Landed in PR [#104](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/104)
  - [x] Balances: `balance`, `transfer` — `pyde::balance(addr_ptr, out_ptr) -> ()` reads the 32-byte address, looks up via `TxOverlay::read_account` (overlay-first, falls through to underlying `AccountStore`), writes 16-byte u128 LE balance to `out_ptr` (0 for missing accounts). `pyde::transfer(to_ptr, amount_ptr) -> i32` reads recipient + u128 amount, then: self-transfer short-circuits to `TRANSFER_OK = 1` (avoids writeback-clobber pattern from standard tx handler); otherwise loads self, checks `balance >= amount` (returns `TRANSFER_INSUFFICIENT = 0` on shortfall), debits self, loads or auto-creates recipient as `AuthKeys::None` funded-unregistered EOA per §11.8 row 13, credits recipient (overflow check), writes both back. Binary success/insufficient flag matches EVM `CALL`'s value-transfer semantics — natural failure case isn't a trap; overflow on the credit IS a trap because it's a programmer bug. Both fns require HostContext.overlay; trap with `"balance host fn called without overlay backend"` if absent. Gas matches EVM: `GAS_BALANCE = 700` (post-EIP-1884 BALANCE; full account-blob fetch), `GAS_TRANSFER = 9_000` (two BALANCE reads + cross-account-write coordination). 9 tests via in-WASM unreachable assertions (balance-unknown returns 0, balance-seeded LE bytes verified, self-transfer short-circuits, insufficient-balance returns 0, transfer-credits-recipient end-to-end with 1000→100 transfer + recipient balance read-back, balance-without-overlay traps) + 3 unit tests (register + duplicate + constants pin). Landed in PR [#106](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/106)
  - [x] Context: `caller`, `origin`, `self_address`, `block_height`, `wave_id`, `block_timestamp`, `chain_id` — shipped alongside the shared `mem::{caller_memory, write_to_memory, read_from_memory}` linear-memory I/O helpers (bounds-checked against the contract's exported `"memory"`; reused by every subsequent host fn). Address-shaped fns (`caller`, `origin`, `self_address`) write 32 bytes to a contract-supplied `out_ptr`; scalar fns (`wave_id`, `block_height`, `block_timestamp`, `chain_id`) return `i64`. `block_height` aliases `wave_id` for EVM-shape ABI portability. `caller` returns `tx.from` at the top-level call (cross-call PR pushes a per-frame caller stack later). Per-call gas charged via `Caller::get_fuel + set_fuel` (wasmtime exposes no single `consume_fuel`); `GAS_CONTEXT_ADDRESS = 5`, `GAS_CONTEXT_SCALAR = 2` per `HOST_FN_ABI §10` "very cheap" tier; out-of-budget surfaces as explicit `"out of fuel: needed N, have M"` trap. 11 tests: registration + duplicate-error path + gas-constant pin + end-to-end via in-WASM `unreachable`-on-mismatch assertions for each fn + 100-iteration loop verifies ≥200 gas tally + 1-gas budget triggers OOF trap inside host fn. Landed in PR [#96](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/96) — **⚠️ Superseded 2026-05-28** by [engine#151](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/151): `block_height` registration dropped (was an EVM-portability alias; redundant with `wave_id`), `block_timestamp` renamed to `wave_timestamp`. Current registered context surface is **6 fns**: `caller`, `origin`, `self_address`, `wave_id`, `wave_timestamp`, `chain_id`. Internal `BlockContext.block_timestamp` struct field intentionally kept (deferred cleanup; only the WASM export name was renamed).
  - [x] Tx context: `tx_hash`, `tx_value`, `tx_gas_remaining`, `calldata_size`, `calldata_copy` — `tx_hash(out_ptr)` (writes 32-byte Poseidon2 tx hash), `tx_value(out_ptr)` (writes u128 as 16 LE bytes — WASM has no native i128), `tx_gas_remaining() -> i64` (post-charge gas via `fuel_to_gas(get_fuel)`) charge `GAS_CONTEXT_ADDRESS = 5` / `GAS_CONTEXT_SCALAR = 2`, landed in PR [#99](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/99). **Calldata fns (PR [#110](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/110))**: added `TxContext.input: Vec<u8>` field to plumb tx.data through to contracts. `pyde::calldata_size() -> i32` returns length directly (scalar; 2 gas). `pyde::calldata_copy(out_ptr, out_len_ptr) -> i32` follows spec §3.3 `out_ptr + out_len_ptr` convention for variable-size output: contract pre-writes its max-bytes-i-can-accept to `*out_len_ptr` (u32 LE); host reads that limit, copies `min(limit, calldata.len())` bytes to out_ptr, updates `*out_len_ptr` with **actual** length (lets contract detect truncation: `actual > limit` → retry with bigger buffer); returns 0 on success. Gas: 5 base + 1/byte copied. Closes the empty-`func.call(&[], &mut [])`-args gap honestly per `HOST_FN_ABI §3.5.2` — default entry IS void-void; contracts read calldata via these host fns. 7 tests: register + duplicate + constants pin + end-to-end via in-WASM unreachable (`calldata_size` returns 5 for [1..=5] input, copy writes "hello" with len reported back, copy truncates at limit=3 reporting actual=10, empty input returns 0).
  - [x] Events: `emit_event` (multi-topic; 1-4 topics; spec §7.5) — `pyde::emit_event(topics_ptr, topic_count, data_ptr, data_len) -> ()` reads `topic_count × 32` topic bytes from contract memory, then `data_len` data bytes, and appends `EmittedEvent { contract: self_address, topics, data }` to the in-flight `HostContext::events` buffer (returned via `CallOutcome::events`; higher-layer pipeline flushes to the state crate's `events_cf` on tx success, drops on revert). Validation: `MAX_TOPICS = 4` (matches EVM `LOG0..LOG4` indexing semantics — 5+ traps), `MAX_EVENT_DATA_BYTES = 8 KB` pre-allocation guard before the gas check fires. Gas: `GAS_EVENT_BASE = 375 + GAS_EVENT_PER_TOPIC = 375 × topic_count + GAS_EVENT_PER_BYTE = 8 × data_len` — same shape as EVM `LOG` so cross-chain devs have the same mental model. Cross-call revert semantics (sub-call frame drops its own events; parent's events survive) need stack-structured buffers; v1 flat buffer is fine because cross-call doesn't ship yet. 8 tests: register + duplicate-error, gas-cost components, constants pin, end-to-end via in-WASM fill-memory + emit verifies events.len() + topic + data + contract = self_address, too-many-topics trap, oversize-data trap. Landed in PR [#101](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/101)
  - [x] Hashing: `hash_blake3`, `hash_poseidon2`, `hash_keccak256` — three host fns sharing the `(in_ptr, in_len, out_ptr) -> ()` shape; each reads input from contract memory, computes a 32-byte digest, writes back. Kept distinct because each serves a different workload: Blake3 for high-throughput commitments (matches Pyde's internal JMT/snapshot/Merkle), Poseidon2 for SNARK-friendly digests (matches Pyde's address/tx-hash/state-root), Keccak-256 for EVM-shape interop. Shared `charge_and_read` preamble: rejects negative len, hard-caps at `MAX_HASH_INPUT_BYTES = 1 MB` (pre-allocation guard before the gas check fires), charges via `get_fuel + set_fuel`. Gas: `GAS_HASH_BASE = 30 + GAS_HASH_PER_WORD = 6` per 32-byte ceiling-divided word; same constants for all three (spec §10 anchors hashing at one tier so authors pick by suitability not gas). Adds `tiny-keccak` workspace dep; `pyde-crypto::poseidon2::poseidon2_hash` already available. 9 tests: register + duplicate-error path, gas-cost word-boundary table (0/1/32/33/64/1024), max-input cost pin (~197K gas), constants pin, end-to-end verification via in-WASM `unreachable`-on-mismatch with hand-computed expected digests for all 3 fns, oversize input traps. Landed in PR [#98](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/98)
  - [x] Crypto: `falcon_verify` — `pyde::falcon_verify(pk_ptr, msg_ptr, msg_len, sig_ptr, sig_len) -> i32` reads a 897-byte FALCON-512 pubkey + variable-len msg + variable-len sig from contract memory, calls `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_verify` natively (~1ms; ~50× faster than a WASM impl because Cranelift can't auto-vectorize the polynomial arithmetic), returns `i32` (1 = valid, 0 = invalid). Length contracts: pk fixed at 897 (no parameter — invariant), `MAX_FALCON_MSG_BYTES = 64 KB`, `MAX_FALCON_SIG_BYTES = 1000` (matches pyde-crypto's accepted upper bound — sigs average ~666 with real-world max 800-900). Gas: flat `GAS_FALCON_VERIFY = 50_000` charged up front (verification cost dominated by polynomial inverse + FFT, both message-length-independent). Invalid-input vs invalid-signature semantics: malformed pubkey, malformed sig (length outside `[500, 1000]`), or oversize inputs all **trap** with descriptive messages; well-formed inputs whose signature doesn't verify return `0` (no trap). The contract gets a binary "valid or not" only when both inputs are structurally well-formed. 8 tests: register + duplicate-error, constants pin, real-keypair end-to-end (keygen + sign + WAT data segments with inlined bytes + in-WASM unreachable on != 1 + ≥50K gas charge), tampered-sig returns 0, oversize-msg trap, oversize-sig trap, malformed-sig-length trap. Landed in PR [#102](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/102)
  - [x] Cross-call: `cross_call`, `cross_call_static` (FREE; bounded by `VIEW_FUEL_CAP`), `delegate_call` — **all three shipped.** `cross_call` (PR [#111](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/111)) per HOST_FN_ABI §7.8 signature: `(target_ptr, fn_name_ptr, fn_name_len, calldata_ptr, calldata_len, value_ptr, gas_limit, return_data_out_ptr, return_data_out_len_ptr) -> i32`. 11-step execution flow: bounds + depth check (`MAX_CROSS_CALL_DEPTH = 1024`, matches EVM) → base gas (`1000 + 8/byte`) → read params from contract memory → look up callee via overlay → value-transfer pre-step **in parent frame** (debit self + credit callee with auto-create AuthKeys::None EOA; survives sub-call revert because it's in parent's overlay layer) → push sub-call overlay layer → build sub-`HostContext` (depth+1, self_address=target, input=calldata, gas_limit=min(forwarded, parent_remaining), fresh return_data + events) → recursive `WasmExecutor::execute_call` → outcome-driven overlay pop (`HaltKind::Return` or clean fn-return → `pop_and_commit`; `HaltKind::Revert`/`Trap` → `pop_and_discard`) → gas deduction from parent fuel by `outcome.consumed_gas` regardless of outcome → return-data copy via spec §3.3 `out_ptr + out_len_ptr` convention. `HostContext` gained `executor: Option<WasmExecutor>` field + `with_executor` builder (cheap clone, Engine + ModuleCache internally Arc'd). Code-hash lookup type-puns `Account.code_hash` (Poseidon2Hash) as Blake3Hash bytes (32-byte newtype byte-pun; documented integration gap until β.3 deploy handler unifies). Deferred from v1 (all need ContractAbi parser): `pyde.abi` selector dispatch, reentrancy guard, access-list enforcement, `#[payable]` attribute check. 7 tests (register + duplicate + 10-constant pin + end-to-end via in-WASM: unknown-target returns 0 no-code path, value-transfer to no-code credits recipient with 100, **real callee E2E** [deploy callee that returns "OK!" + deploy caller that cross_calls + byte-verify return_data], no-overlay traps). **`cross_call_static` shipped** (PR [#117](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/117)) per HOST_FN_ABI §7.8 signature: `(target_ptr, fn_name_ptr, fn_name_len, calldata_ptr, calldata_len, gas_limit, return_data_out_ptr, return_data_out_len_ptr) -> i32` — 8 params (drops `value_ptr` vs `cross_call`). Read-only nested-call host fn. `HostContext` gained `view_mode: bool` field + `with_view_mode` builder. Mutating host fns (`sstore`, `sdelete`, `transfer`, `emit_event`) now trap with `ERR_FORBIDDEN` when `caller.data().view_mode` is true — runtime check is the definitive guarantee per §3.7 (catches mutations even if static call-graph check is bypassed via `call_indirect`). `cross_call_static` execution: bounds + depth check → flat `GAS_CROSS_CALL_STATIC_BASE = 50` dispatch gas (sub-call execution itself is FREE to caller per spec §7.8 — view calls have no economic incentive to charge) → read target + fn_name + calldata → look up callee account → push overlay layer (defensive — always discarded on exit since view calls shouldn't mutate) → build sub-`HostContext` (depth+1, `view_mode=true`, `value=0`, `gas_limit = VIEW_FUEL_CAP = 10M ≈ 3ms wall-clock per spec; bounds wall-clock not economics) → recursive `WasmExecutor::execute_call` → outcome classification (Return → 0; Trap with "out of fuel" → `ERR_CROSS_CALL_OUT_OF_GAS = -11`; other Trap → `ERR_CROSS_CALL_FAILED = -8`) → return-data copy. `#[view]` attribute dispatch-time check **deferred**: runtime `view_mode` flag is the definitive guarantee; non-view contracts called via `cross_call_static` will trap at first mutation attempt (sstore/sdelete/transfer/emit_event). Wires onto PR-16's ABI parser when ModuleCache v2 carries `(Module, ContractAbi)`. 11 new tests (3 cross_call_static E2E: success / mutation-trap / no-code-callee; 4 direct view-mode-blocks for each mutating host fn; 1 direct view-mode-allows-sload; 3 unit: register / duplicate / constants pin). **`delegate_call` shipped** (PR [#118](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/118)) per HOST_FN_ABI §7.8 — 8 params (same shape as `cross_call_static`; drops `value_ptr` because caller's value flows through unchanged). Runs target's compiled WASM in CALLER's identity + storage + value context (EVM DELEGATECALL equivalent). Sub-context: code looked up by `target_ptr` but `self_address = caller's self_address` — every `sstore`/`sload`/`self_address()` in sub-call sees caller's frame. `tx.value` preserved as caller's value (no transfer pre-step). `view_mode` propagates from caller. Gas: `GAS_DELEGATE_CALL_BASE = 1000` + `GAS_DELEGATE_CALL_PER_BYTE = 8` × calldata_len + sub-call's `consumed_gas` regardless of outcome. Overlay handling identical to `cross_call`: Return → commit; Revert/Trap → discard. Foundation for proxy + upgrade patterns. **Security note documented**: callee's code gets direct write access to caller's storage; authors must trust callee completely. `#[delegate_safe]` attribute deferred (auditors flag as standard practice). 3 new tests (sub-call self_address verified equal to caller's via in-WASM `pyde::self_address` + return + byte-check; ERR_CALLEE_NOT_FOUND for no-code target; no-overlay trap) + 3 unit (register / duplicate / constants pin). 194/194 wasm-exec tests passing. PR-15 cross-call trio complete.
  - [x] Halt: `return`, `revert` — `pyde::return(ptr, len) -> !` + `pyde::revert(ptr, len) -> !`. Both halt contract execution and write `len` bytes from contract memory at `ptr` into `HostContext.return_data` (new field); executor reads it off the recovered context and surfaces as `CallOutcome.return_data`. Distinct sentinel prefixes in the trap message (`pyde::return: N bytes` / `pyde::revert: N bytes`) let the executor classify into `CallOutcome.halt_kind: Option<HaltKind>` — `Some(Return)` (state survives — tx pipeline finalizes on success), `Some(Revert)` (state discarded — overlay frame drops), `Some(Trap)` (generic — unreachable / OOF / host-fn error / divide-by-zero), `None` (clean fn-return path). Higher layers use the discriminator to drive overlay frame commit-vs-discard. Why trap instead of typed result: WASM functions have typed return signatures; making return/revert return-the-function would force every contract entry point to carry the same shape — trap-based halt lets any signature work, with halt info threaded out-of-band through the trap message + return_data buffer. `MAX_RETURN_DATA_BYTES = 16 KB` pre-allocation guard; gas essentially free (5 base + 1/byte). Foundation for cross-call (PR-14): cross-call needs `halt_kind` to decide overlay commit/discard. 8 tests: register + duplicate + constants pin (3 unit) + end-to-end via in-WASM construction (return surfaces "hello", revert surfaces "fail", clean return yields None, unreachable classifies as Trap, oversize triggers data-too-large trap). Landed in PR [#107](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/107)
  - [x] Gas: `consume_gas` — explicit manual gas burn. `consume_gas(amount: i64)` charges `amount` gas immediately; no-op on negative/zero (spec treats negative as "ignore"); out-of-fuel trap if budget can't cover. No host-fn dispatch surcharge — `consume_gas` IS the metering primitive, not an instance of metered code. Useful for contracts that want to deliberately spend gas (e.g., delay loops, fairness mechanisms). Landed in PR [#99](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/99)
  - [x] Randomness: `beacon_get` — `pyde::beacon_get(out_ptr) -> i32` writes the wave's committee-derived VRF beacon (32 bytes) to out_ptr; returns 0 always. Per HOST_FN_ABI §7.11. `BlockContext` gained `beacon: [u8; 32]` field (sourced from γ.1 consensus; XOR of all committee members' beacon shares from the prior anchor round — deterministic + identical across all validators on the same wave). Gas: `GAS_BEACON_GET = 50` (small base; no computation needed — host fn just copies the pre-computed value from HostContext). Adversary model documented: beacon is publicly predictable WITHIN the wave (adversaries observe it the moment the prior anchor commits, before the current wave's txs run) — safe from validators biasing it (committee-XOR construction) but NOT safe from same-wave adversaries exploiting it. For adversary-private randomness, contracts should use the threshold-encryption pipeline (commit beacon-encrypted tx, reveal in later wave) — higher-layer protocol, not a host fn. 5 tests: register + duplicate + constants pin (3 unit) + end-to-end via in-WASM (0xBE-filled beacon writes 0xBE at byte 0 + byte 31; default-zero beacon writes all zeros). Landed in PR [#113](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/113)
  - [ ] Parachain extensions (gated): `parachain_storage_read`/`write`/`delete`, `parachain_emit_event`, `parachain_id`, `parachain_version`, `send_xparachain_message`, `threshold_encrypt`, `threshold_decrypt`
- [x] Deploy-time validation (3-layer per `HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC §3.7`) — **partial: 3 of 5 layers shipped** (PR [#116](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/116)). New `crates/wasm-exec/src/deploy.rs` ships `validate_deploy(wasm) -> Result<ContractAbi, DeployError>` running: **Layer 1 schema** (`pyde_abi_version ≤ MAX_SUPPORTED_ABI_VERSION = ContractAbi::V1_0`; Borsh decode succeeds), **Layer 2 cross-reference** (every `FunctionAbi.name` has a matching WASM func export; reverse-direction "every WASM export covered by ABI" deferred — spec leaves "internal helpers TBD how to mark"), **Layer 3 attribute compatibility** (full §3.5.1 negative table: view+payable, view+constructor, view+reentrant, view+sponsored, view+fallback, view+receive, constructor+reentrant, constructor+sponsored, constructor+fallback, constructor+receive, receive without payable, receive+reentrant, fallback+receive on same fn; plus at-most-one fallback/receive + dispatch-index in-bounds + dispatch-index attr-match validation). `DeployError` taxonomy gives wallets + otigen a precise per-layer reason: MissingAbiSection, DuplicateAbiSection, AbiDecode, UnsupportedAbiVersion, WasmParse, DeclaredFnMissingFromWasm, IncompatibleAttributes, MultipleDispatchFunctions, DispatchIndexAttrMismatch, DispatchIndexOutOfBounds. **Deferred**: Layer 4 static call-graph view-enforcement + Layer 5 static access-list (both need WASM call-graph walking; runtime view_mode flag + access-list slot check are the definitive guarantees per spec). Wasmparser 0.244 pinned matching wasmtime 26's bundled version to avoid duplicate transitive copies. 15 tests covering happy path + every error variant + extra-WASM-exports-allowed semantics. Reuses the comprehensive `types/abi.rs` `ContractAbi` (already had `name + version + events + parachain_imports` extension fields beyond spec minimum).
- [x] Attribute application + `pyde.abi` custom-section extraction — `extract_pyde_abi(wasm)` walks the WASM binary via wasmparser, finds the single `"pyde.abi"` custom section (rejects missing/duplicate), Borsh-decodes to `ContractAbi`. Attribute application: **`#[view]` runtime mode flag now wired** (PR [#117](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/117) — `HostContext.view_mode` + mutating host fns trap with ERR_FORBIDDEN; reached via `cross_call_static`). **`#[payable]` value-transfer check + `#[constructor]` lockout + `#[reentrant]` guard still pending** (need ContractAbi lookup at dispatch time → blocked on ModuleCache v2 carrying `(Module, ContractAbi)`). The static side of deploy-time validation IS shipped (attribute compatibility per §3.5.1). Landed alongside PR [#116](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/116)
- [x] Implement `Executor` trait (from `interfaces`) — `WasmExecutorAdapter` in `crates/wasm-exec/src/executor_impl.rs` wraps `WasmExecutor` and dispatches based on `tx.tx_type`: routes `Standard`/`RegisterPubkey`/`EmergencyPause`/`EmergencyResume`/`MultisigTx`/`RotateMultisig`/`ClaimAirdrop`/`SweepAirdrop`/`StakeDeposit`/`StakeWithdraw`/`ClaimReward`/`Slash` to the corresponding β.3 handler; `Deploy` + `ContractCall` paths placeholder until full call-stack pipeline finalizes. Failed handlers map to `gas_used = MIN_GAS_LIMIT` (21K intrinsic floor) and `ReceiptStatus::Reverted` per spec §10.4 ("state changes rolled back; gas IS still charged for the work done"). Closes β.4 → β.3 contract surface. PR [#114](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/114)

#### β.5 `mempool` crate `[PAR within β] → β.3`
- [x] Scaffold + core data structures + dedup-only admission — opens β.5 (PR [#121](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/121)). `Mempool` struct: `by_hash: HashMap<TxHash, Arc<Tx>>` (primary dedup) + `by_sender: HashMap<Address, BTreeMap<u64, TxHash>>` (per-sender nonce-ordered FIFO); single `parking_lot::Mutex` guards both (correctness-first; sharding deferred to profiling evidence). `MempoolConfig { max_size, max_per_sender }` defaults 50_000 / 64 (aligned with the 16-slot nonce window + headroom for replacement). `AdmissionError` taxonomy distinguishes permanent rejects (`DuplicateNonce`) from transient ones (`PoolFull`, `SenderCapReached`); `AdmissionOutcome::AlreadyKnown` separates idempotent re-admission from errors. `MempoolStats { admitted, already_known, rejected_permanent, rejected_transient, removed }` snapshot via `stats()`. Public API: `new` / `admit` / `remove` / `remove_all_by_sender` / `contains` / `fetch` / `len` / `is_empty` / `stats` / `config`. **PR-1 admission scope is dedup + capacity ONLY** — chain_id / nonce window / balance / gas bounds / calldata size / attribute coherence land in PR-2; FALCON sig verify in PR-3; replacement-by-fee deferred to v2. 11 tests covering: empty default / admit + dedup / dup-nonce reject / pool-full reject / per-sender-cap reject + other-sender-unaffected / remove drops both indexes / remove-missing returns None / remove_all_by_sender / fetch clones / config defaults / config builders.
- [x] FALCON-512 verify pipeline — PR [#124](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/124) adds FALCON sig verify as **step 8 (last)** of the admission pipeline. Most expensive single check (~1ms per sig per `pyde-crypto` measurements) — runs only after all cheap checks pass, so bad-format / wrong-chain / overdrawn txs reject without paying FALCON cost. `admit()` now takes `sender_auth_keys: &AuthKeys` and dispatches via β.3's `verify_tx_against_auth` (handles `Single` + `MultiSig` + `None` variants). **Bootstrap exemption**: `tx_type=RegisterPubkey` skips FALCON entirely per Ch 11 §11.8 row 13 (those txs CREATE the sender's auth keys — by construction they can't have valid keys yet). New `AdmissionError` variants: `AuthKeysMissing` (permanent — sender is `AuthKeys::None` AND tx isn't RegisterPubkey; the user should submit RegisterPubkey first) and `SignatureInvalid` (permanent — `verify_tx_against_auth` returned false; verify-errors collapsed into the same code since the caller can't act on the distinction). **Batched verify deferred to a follow-up**: v1 admits per-tx (gossip + RPC paths arrive per-tx); batch verify becomes load-bearing only if gossip starts shipping multi-tx packs. Pyde-crypto exposes `falcon_verify_all` for that future PR. 4 new FALCON-path tests (`auth_keys_missing_rejects_non_register_pubkey`, `signature_invalid_rejects_against_real_pubkey`, `register_pubkey_skips_falcon_with_none_auth_keys`, `falcon_runs_after_cheaper_checks_short_circuit` proving structural fails at step 4 short-circuit before step 8) + test helpers `admit_skip_falcon` / `as_register_pubkey` to keep pre-existing pool-bookkeeping tests working without a real FALCON keypair. 25/25 mempool tests passing.
- [x] Validation rules: chain_id, nonce window, balance, gas bounds, calldata size, attribute coherence — PR [#122](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/122) extends `admit()` to take `(tx, state_balance, state_nonce_window, base_fee)` and runs the full structural + state-checked pipeline. Validation order (cheapest first; each failure short-circuits): (1) dedup by hash, (2) pool/sender capacity, (3) duplicate-nonce in-pool, (4) **structural** via β.3's `validate_tx_structure` (gas bounds `[MIN_GAS_LIMIT, BLOCK_GAS_MAX]` + calldata ≤ `MAX_CALLDATA = 64 KB` + encoded size ≤ `MAX_TX_SIZE = 128 KB` + sig presence + per-tx-type shape covering `to=ZERO` for envelope/deploy, `value=0 + empty sig` for `RegisterPubkey`, etc.), (5) `chain_id` match (new `MempoolConfig.chain_id` default `1 = mainnet`), (6) `NonceWindow::is_acceptable` (catches below-base + above-window-of-16 + already-consumed-bit), (7) balance reservation `value + gas_limit × base_fee` (saturating u128 math). Caller supplies the state-dependent inputs — Mempool itself stays **sync** (async-vs-sync concern lives at the caller boundary; MempoolView impl uses async StateView in PR-6, gossip/RPC paths pre-fetch). New `AdmissionError` variants: `StructuralInvalid(TxValidationError)` (permanent — wraps β.3 taxonomy giving wallets a precise per-rule reason), `WrongChainId { actual, expected }` (permanent), `NonceNotAcceptable { nonce, window_base }` (permanent in v1; v2 may split out a transient "too-high" variant if a deferred-queue lands), `InsufficientBalance { have, need }` (transient — balance may rise via incoming transfers). 10 new tests covering each new failure mode + happy-path state-dependent admit + balance-exactly-covers-reservation edge case + structural-gas-too-low + structural-calldata-too-large. 21/21 mempool tests passing.
- [x] Gossip admission (integration with γ's `net` crate via `NetworkView` trait) — **β-side scaffolding shipped; γ wiring happens at MC-2 binary assembly.** PR [#127](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/127) ships the per-source admit surface so MC-2 can plug γ.2's `net` crate in as plumbing without touching `pyde-engine-interfaces` (frozen). New `Source` enum (`Rpc` / `Gossip`); `Mempool::admit_local` / `admit_gossiped` / `admit_with_source(...)` all delegate to the existing `admit()` and bump per-source stats only on `Admitted` outcomes. New `MempoolStats.admitted_local` + `admitted_gossiped` subsets of `admitted`. Critically: gossip-replay of an RPC-submitted tx (already in the pool) returns `AlreadyKnown` and does NOT bump `admitted_gossiped` — honest gossip cross-pollination doesn't spuriously inflate the counter. **NetworkView left untouched** because `pyde-engine-interfaces` is frozen; the tx-gossip topic + inbound dispatch lives in γ.2 and connects at MC-2 (γ calls `mempool.admit_gossiped()` on receive). The β.5 BAR ("replay a tx end-to-end against `MockNetwork`") will be exercised at MC-2 once γ.2's tx-gossip ships; the call surface needed is now in place. 4 new tests: `admit_local_increments_local_counter`, `admit_gossiped_increments_gossiped_counter`, `already_known_does_not_increment_source_counter` (the critical gossip-replay non-double-count), `rejected_admission_does_not_increment_source_counter`. 33/33 mempool tests passing.
- [x] Per-sender rate limit + concurrent cap (DDoS protection) — PR [#125](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/125) ships per-sender token-bucket rate limiting as **step 2 of admission** (between dedup and capacity). `MempoolConfig.rate_per_sec` (default 10/s) + `rate_burst` (default 20) define the bucket; lazy refill on access via `tokens = min(tokens + elapsed × rate, burst)`. **Counted AFTER dedup** — re-submitting the same tx hash returns `AlreadyKnown` and does NOT drain tokens (honest gossip-replay isn't penalised). New `AdmissionError::RateLimited { rate_per_sec, burst }` (transient). New `MempoolStats.rate_limited` counter (subset of `rejected_transient`) — operators distinguish "pool full" pressure from "spammer here" pressure. `Eq` derive dropped from `AdmissionError` (f64 doesn't impl Eq); `PartialEq` retained so tests still use `==` where the variant has no float field. Concurrent-cap already covered by `max_per_sender` from PR-1 — the spec lumps them in one row but they target different attack vectors (rate vs depth); both are now in place. 5 new tests: burst overflow, per-sender independence, already-known doesn't drain, token-bucket math (unit test of the refill formula — avoids wall-clock flakiness), config builders extended. 29/29 mempool tests passing.
- [x] Implement `MempoolView` trait (from `interfaces`) — **β.5 milestone closed.** PR [#129](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/129) ships `PydeMempoolView` wrapping `Mempool` + `Arc<dyn StateView>` + `Arc<RwLock<u128>>` for base_fee. Async-adapts the sync `admit()` to the async trait surface by pre-fetching `balance` / `nonce_window` / `auth_keys` via the StateView handle, then calling `admit_gossiped` (trait route assumed gossip; RPC layers bypass the trait and call `Mempool::admit_local` directly to get the `admitted_local` counter). `AdmissionError → InterfaceError` map: `Refused` for permanent application-layer rejects (AlreadyKnown / DuplicateNonce / WrongChainId / NonceNotAcceptable / SignatureInvalid / AuthKeysMissing); `InvalidInput` for `StructuralInvalid`; `Storage` (= retryable per trait taxonomy) for transient rejects (PoolFull / SenderCapReached / InsufficientBalance / RateLimited). **`drain_for_batch` v1 selector**: ascending-nonce-per-sender FIFO, greedy fill to `max_bytes`; single oversize tx still returned when cap < its size (the `!out.is_empty()` short-circuit handles the < MAX_TX_SIZE edge case). Priority-fee ordering deferred to a follow-up if MEV-protection metrics show it's load-bearing. **base_fee management**: `update_base_fee(new)` called after each wave commit; `base_fee()` snapshot read; `mempool()` exposes the inner `Mempool` so RPC paths can call `admit_local` directly for `admitted_local` accounting. 10 new mempool_view tests (insert happy path, already-known ok, Refused on permanent reject, InvalidInput on structural, contains + fetch via trait, drain happy path, drain respects max_bytes, drain-zero edge case, update_base_fee, fetch-missing returns None). 43/43 mempool tests passing. **β.5 BAR substantively met — the `MockNetwork`-driven end-to-end test ("replay a tx end-to-end against in-memory `MockNetwork`") lives at MC-2 binary assembly once γ.2's net crate is wired in; the call surface needed for that wiring is now complete on the β side.**

- [x] **β.5 post-milestone follow-ups** — five PRs landed AFTER the β.5 milestone-closeout that materially harden the β-side surface for MC-2 wire-up: **cross-β integration tests** PR [#139](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/139) (admit → drain → execute on real RocksDB through `PydeMempoolView` + `WasmExecutorAdapter` — RegisterPubkey bootstrap path + Deploy direct-execute + multi-tx drain max_bytes); **real-FALCON e2e** PR [#140](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/140) closing the gap flagged on #139 — generates a real FALCON keypair via pyde-crypto, signs a Standard transfer tx, admits through `MempoolView::insert` (full FALCON verify, NOT bootstrap exemption), drains, executes, verifies sender debited + recipient auto-created + nonce committed; companion negative-path test asserts bogus sig → `InterfaceError::Refused`; **criterion benches on mempool hot paths** PR [#142](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/142) measures admit_local FALCON-signed at 31.5 µs (31.6K admits/s ST), admit_local RegisterPubkey-bootstrap-exempt at 20.3 µs (49.2K admits/s ST), drain_for_batch at 28 µs / 304 µs / 5.8 ms for 100 / 1K / 10K txs respectively — **corrects the prior "FALCON verify ~1 ms per sig" assumption (actual: ~11.2 µs differential, off by ~40×)** and establishes that drain double-encode-borsh is sub-millisecond noise below 1K txs/batch; **criterion benches on executor hot paths** PR [#144](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/144) measures execute_tx Standard transfer at 56.2 µs (17.8K tx/s ST) and execute_call minimal void-main WASM at 11.1 µs (90.4K calls/s ST) — combined admit + execute pipeline is ~88 µs/tx ST (~11.4K tps), aligning with [[honest_throughput_reset]]'s "10-30K plaintext v1 target" once validator-side parallelism kicks in; **deterministic drain ordering** PR [#145](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/145) sorts `by_sender` keys lex-ascending before iterating in `drain_for_batch` so the returned `Vec<Tx>` is byte-reproducible across runs and across validators — useful for tests, debugging, and any future consensus-side machinery that wants to compare drain outputs (the priority-fee selector I'd previously flagged turned out not to be a v1 feature — `Tx` has no `tip` field; that lives gated on a v2 hard-fork of the frozen types crate). 925 workspace tests passing, 0 failed, 2 `#[ignore]`'d (known γ.15/γ.16 single-producer-quorum tests). The perf-arc total: 4 PRs (#142 / #144 / #145 + the earlier closeouts) where every claim is now backed by numbers, not priors.

**β BAR:** `cargo test` clean on `execution-side` branch; mock-based integration tests (using `interfaces::mock`) pass for state + execution + mempool; can replay a tx end-to-end against the in-memory `MockNetwork`.

### MC-1 Stream γ — Engine Consensus + Network `[PAR within] → MC-0` — `pyde-net/engine` branch `consensus-side`

Implements Chapter 6, `SLASHING.md`, `VALIDATOR_LIFECYCLE.md`, `STATE_SYNC.md`, `CHAIN_HALT.md`, `NETWORK_PROTOCOL.md`.

**Crates owned:** `consensus`, `net`, `dkg`, `slashing`, `node`.

#### γ.1 `consensus` crate `[SEQ within γ]` — foundational
- [x] `Vertex` structure (round, member_id, parent_refs, batch_refs, state_root_sigs, prev_anchor_attestation, decryption_shares, sig) — landed in `types` crate at MC-0
- [x] Local DAG view per validator (`VertexStore`: hash + round + slot indexes, equivocation-aware, `parking_lot::RwLock` guarded) — PR [#1](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/1)
- [x] Canonical `vertex_hash = Blake3(borsh(vertex_sans_falcon_sig))` centralised — PR [#1](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/1)
- [x] Equivocation flagging on insert (`InsertOutcome::Equivocation { prior_at_slot }`; full slashing flow lives in γ.4)
- [x] Vertex production pipeline (`VertexBuilder` + `Signer` trait + `select_parents` helper that skips equivocating slots; returns `(VertexHash, Vertex)` so callers get the dedup key free) — PR [#2](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/2)
- [x] Vertex validation pipeline (`validate_vertex` + `Verifier` trait + `ValidationConfig`; cheapest-first checks: range → batch-dedup → parent quorum → parent-round homogeneity → FALCON sig; `MissingParent` returns hash so caller can fetch and retry) — PR [#3](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/3)
- [x] Round advancement (`RoundTracker`: monotonic counter, distinct-`member_id` quorum check, `try_advance` / `try_advance_to_max` for state-sync catch-up, equivocator-resistant via distinct-producer counting) — PR [#9](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/9)
- [x] Anchor selection: `select_anchor(beacon, round, prev_state_root) -> u32` — Blake3 over `beacon || round.le || prev_state_root.blake3`, then `mod COMMITTEE_SIZE` (= 128, spec-locked, not a parameter). Dual-hash aware (only Blake3 leg mixes in; Poseidon2 reserved for SNARK paths). Uniform at 128 = 2^7 (no rejection sampling needed). Sibling `select_anchor_for_testing(..., committee_size)` exposes the divisor for tests modelling small committees — `pub` only because Cargo can't share `#[cfg(test)]` across crates. — PR [#4](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/4), tightened in PR [#112](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/112)
- [x] **Beacon derivation type surface** — per Ch 6 §9 the "VRF beacon" is actually a threshold-signature beacon (`beacon_N = Hash(combined_threshold_sigs("epoch_N_beacon"))`); the roadmap row's "VRF" naming was loose. New `crates/consensus/src/beacon.rs` ships the trait + types + a `MockBeaconScheme` (Blake3-deterministic) so the consensus layer integrates against a stable surface today, with the production pyde-crypto threshold-sig backend dropping in once pyde-crypto is engine-CI-accessible (same blocker as `MockDkg`). `BeaconScheme` trait: `share` / `verify_share` / `combine`. `BeaconDerivationContext { epoch, previous }`. `BeaconShare { member_id, bytes }`. `BeaconError` (InsufficientShares / DuplicateMember / InvalidShare). `const BEACON_THRESHOLD = 85` (= 2f+1 for f=42 on the 128-member committee — matches the consensus quorum + DKG threshold). Mock derivation: `share = Blake3("pyde:beacon:mock:share:" \|\| prev \|\| epoch \|\| member_id)`, `combine = Blake3("pyde:beacon:mock:combine:" \|\| prev \|\| epoch \|\| sorted_share_bytes)` (sorted by member_id so combination is share-order-independent — matches the spec's "deterministic aggregated signature" property), `genesis_beacon(seed) = Blake3("pyde:beacon:genesis:" \|\| seed)` for the chain's first beacon. 18 tests cover: genesis determinism + seed-variance, mock share determinism + variance across (member, epoch, previous), `verify_share` accepts well-formed / rejects tampered + wrong-member, `combine` rejects below-threshold / duplicate-member / invalid-share, `combine` is share-order-independent + deterministic for same input, `combine` differs per epoch + per previous, epoch-0 derivation chains off `genesis_beacon`. Wiring into `pick_anchor` + anchor-skip rules + production threshold-sig backend land in follow-ups. — PR [#109](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/109)
- [x] **Beacon → wave_committer wiring** — γ.15 PR-2: replaces the wave_committer's "lowest honest member_id" stub with `select_anchor(beacon, round, prev_state_root)` (production-shape, committee size locked at spec 128). Threads `beacon: Beacon` + `prev_state_root: StateRoot` through `WaveCommitterConfig` → `ValidatorRunConfig`; both are static placeholders (`[0u8; 32]` + `StateRoot::EMPTY`) until γ.15 PR-3 (per-epoch beacon derivation flow) + β.3 (real state roots through `StateMutator::commit_wave`) wire real inputs. New picker semantics: target slot derived from beacon → return honest vertex at that slot; `None` if missing (transient — committer waits) or equivocating (production-correct, but waits indefinitely until γ.16 anchor-skip rules ship). Strips the `committee_size` parameter from `select_anchor` entirely (was needed only for testability) — production API is now spec-literal `Hash(beacon, round, prev_state_root) mod 128`. Test path uses `select_anchor_for_testing(..., committee_size)` (in consensus crate) + `pick_anchor_with_committee_size` + `tick_with_committee_size` (in wave_committer) for small-committee scenarios. Pairs with the engine-side `lookback_state_root` → `prev_state_root` rename + the matching pyde-book rename (commit fef9c30 on main, ticked here implicitly via this row). 2 integration tests (`run_commits_waves_at_tick_cadence`, `validator_with_producer_and_committer_commits_waves`) are `#[ignore]`'d because the 1/128 per-round anchor-hit rate under static all-zero beacon + member_id=0 only makes wave commit unreliable without γ.16. Replaced with a sibling `validator_with_producer_and_committer_runs_both_tasks` asserting only on `vertices_produced`. — PR [#112](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/112)
- [x] **Mysticeti anchor-skip rules + ≥85-vote support detection** — γ.16: replaces the wave-committer's "wait forever on missing anchor" semantic with the full 3-stage commit-or-skip decision per Ch 6 §7. New `resolve_anchor(dag, round, beacon, prev_state_root) -> AnchorResolution` returns `Commit(anchor) | Skip | Pending`: computes the target slot via `select_anchor` (γ.15 PR-2), looks up the unique honest vertex there, then runs `check_anchor_support` against `QUORUM = 85` and maps the 3-stage outcome onto the resolution. Missing / equivocating slots apply the same R+1-fill rule — Skip once R+1 reaches quorum, otherwise Pending (no future vertex can rescue a missing anchor with quorum already filled). Tick state machine: on `Commit`, assemble + persist + `sequencer.record_committed`; on `Skip`, advance `next_anchor_round` (NOT `next_wave_id`) + `sequencer.record_skipped` + bump `wave_anchors_skipped` metric; on `Pending`, break and wait. Tick loop now uses `highest_round - 2` as the upper bound (need R+2 to run the certify stage). `WaveCommitter` gains an internal `AnchorSequencer` (orchestrator-wiring of the γ.4 `AnchorSequencer` type from PR [#37](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/37)), exposed via `sequencer()` for tests + a future PR that shares it with the RPC layer (`pyde_getAnchorOutcome`). New `wave_anchors_skipped: AtomicU64` metric (also in `MetricsSnapshot`). Test-only siblings `resolve_anchor_for_testing(..., committee_size, quorum)` + `WaveCommitter::tick_for_testing(state, committee_size, quorum)` let unit tests model small committees (e.g. quorum=3) without spawning 128 producers. 15 tests cover: full-3-stage commit + sequencer record, skip on R+1-full-unsupported / target-slot-empty / target-slot-equivocates, pending on R+1-below-quorum / target-slot-empty-below-quorum, production resolver at full 85-quorum DAG, tick advances through skipped rounds without bumping wave_id, single-anchor-no-R+1 is pending, empty-dag noop, run() exits on shutdown drop. The two `#[ignore]`'d validator integration tests from γ.15 PR-2 stay ignored — under a single producer at `member_id = 0` with the production `QUORUM = 85`, clearing 85 supporters at R+1 is mathematically impossible; they reinstate when multi-validator coordination ships. — PR [#120](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/120)
- [x] **Beacon types + genesis bootstrap** — γ.15 PR-3a: type surface + plumbing for the per-epoch beacon flow. No runtime rotation yet — every wave commits under the same chain-globally-agreed genesis beacon, so PR-3b (gossip topic + share buffer) and PR-3c (epoch state machine + combine + publish) have a stable shape to wire against. New types in `crates/types/src/consensus.rs`: `pub type Epoch = u64` (sibling to `Round` / `WaveId`), `pub const BEACON_LEN: usize = 32` + `pub type Beacon = [u8; BEACON_LEN]` (migrated up from `pyde_engine_consensus::anchor`, which now `pub use`s them so the historic import path stays valid), `pub const GENESIS_BEACON_SEED: &[u8] = b"pyde:genesis:beacon:v1"` (chain-wide consensus parameter; v1 hardcodes it, governance ratification lands with the genesis-block surface). `WaveCommitRecord` gains two wire-format fields: `epoch: Epoch` (every wave carries its epoch) and `next_epoch_beacon: Option<Beacon>` (populated only on the last wave of each epoch per Ch 6 §9 step 4 — `None` everywhere else). `WaveCommitInputs` mirrors both; every initializer across the workspace updated (12 files). `WaveCommitterConfig::default()` derives `beacon` from `genesis_beacon(GENESIS_BEACON_SEED)` instead of the previous `[0u8; BEACON_LEN]` placeholder — every validator derives the same chain-derived value at bootstrap. — PR [#123](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/123)
- [x] **Beacon-shares gossip topic + buffer** — γ.15 PR-3b: receive-side plumbing. `BeaconShare` becomes wire-stable (`epoch: Epoch` field + `BorshSerialize`/`BorshDeserialize` derives); `MockBeaconScheme::verify_share` now rejects shares carrying a mismatched epoch. New `pyde/beacon-shares/1` gossip topic (`pyde_engine_net::topics::BEACON_SHARES`) added to `topics::ALL`. New `BeaconShareBuffer` (`crates/node/src/beacon_buffer.rs`) — `Arc<RwLock<HashMap<Epoch, HashMap<u32, BeaconShare>>>>` with `insert` (returns `New | Duplicate`), `count(epoch)`, `quorum_reached(epoch, threshold)`, `shares_for_epoch(epoch)`, `prune_epoch`, `total`, `clear`. `ValidatorMainLoop` constructs an internal `Arc<BeaconShareBuffer>` exposed via `beacon_buffer()`; `dispatch` gains a `beacon_buffer: &BeaconShareBuffer` arg + a topic branch that borsh-decodes incoming shares and inserts them, with per-outcome metric bumps. Four new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`beacon_shares_received`, `beacon_shares_buffered`, `beacon_share_duplicates`, `beacon_share_decode_failures`) surfaced through `MetricsSnapshot`. 18 new tests across consensus (epoch-mismatch verify rejection), net topics (BEACON_SHARES wire-pin), node beacon_buffer (10 tests covering insert / dedupe / count / quorum / prune / clear), and node mainloop dispatch (4 tests covering successful decode + buffer, duplicate accounting, malformed-bytes decode-failure path, and distinct-member parallel inserts). No signature verification yet — PR-3c adds the FALCON-pubkey-vs-committee verify pass before buffering. No combine trigger or epoch-advancement logic — also PR-3c. — PR [#126](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/126)
- [x] **Epoch helpers + BeaconStore** — γ.15 PR-3c.1: types-only slice of the original PR-3c (split mid-stream into 3c.1 + 3c.2 for review-ability — the full thing was getting too big for one PR). New constants + helpers in `crates/types/src/consensus.rs`: `pub const EPOCH_LENGTH_WAVES: WaveId = 100` (chain-wide rotation cadence; v1 hardcoded, governance ratification with the genesis-block surface), `epoch_for_wave(wave_id, epoch_length) -> (Epoch, WaveId)` (pure partition helper — panics on `epoch_length == 0`), and `is_last_wave_of_epoch(wave_id, epoch_length) -> bool` (detects the Ch 6 §9 step 4 publish boundary). New `BeaconStore` (`crates/node/src/beacon_store.rs`) — `Arc<RwLock<HashMap<Epoch, Beacon>>>` cache of per-epoch derived beacons + a `genesis: Beacon` pre-computed via `genesis_beacon(GENESIS_BEACON_SEED)` at construction so every validator agrees on the epoch-0 fallback. API: `new`, `put(epoch, beacon)`, `get(epoch)`, `current(epoch)` (stored value → genesis fallback for epoch 0 only → `None` for an un-derived later epoch — caller waits), `genesis()`, `len`/`is_empty`/`clear`. 12 new tests pin the constants + cover partition boundaries / panic paths / read-write roundtrip / genesis fallback rule / cross-instance determinism / overwrite semantics / clear-keeps-genesis. **No behaviour change** today — the cache stays empty in production because nothing populates it yet. PR-3c.2 ships the dynamic flow: `NetworkView::publish_beacon_share` API, share-emit task at each wave commit, combine trigger when buffer reaches quorum, wave-committer swap-over to read from `BeaconStore`, and `WaveCommitRecord.next_epoch_beacon` populated at epoch boundaries. — PR [#128](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/128)
- [x] **Beacon share-emit + NetworkView::publish_beacon_share** — γ.15 PR-3c.2: consumer-side of the per-epoch beacon flow (PR-3c was further split into 3c.2 + 3c.3 mid-stream — the combine trigger + wave-committer swap-over + `WaveCommitRecord.next_epoch_beacon` publish moved to 3c.3 so each PR stays reviewable). Two new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`beacon_shares_emitted`, `beacon_share_publish_failures`) + matching `MetricsSnapshot` fields. Vertex-producer test impls (`RecordingNetwork`, `FailingNetwork`) extended to satisfy the updated trait. - [x] **Beacon combine + swap-over + WaveCommitRecord publish — loop closed** — γ.15 PR-3c.3: the per-epoch beacon rotation is now end-to-end. Three discrete edits in `wave_committer.rs`: (1) **Combine trigger** — new `maybe_combine_next_epoch_beacon(state, threshold)` helper fires after the share-emit hook on every commit; checks `BeaconShareBuffer.quorum_reached(next_epoch, QUORUM)`, pulls shares via `shares_for_epoch`, calls `BeaconScheme::combine` with `BeaconDerivationContext { epoch: next_epoch, previous: beacon_store.current(committed_epoch) }`, stores result in `BeaconStore`, prunes buffer. Idempotent — store-presence check short-circuits subsequent triggers for the same epoch. (2) **Anchor-selection swap-over** — `tick_with_resolver` derives `live_beacon = beacon_store.current(epoch_for_wave(state.next_wave_id))` per tick instead of `&self.config.beacon`. For epoch 0 the store returns the genesis fallback; for later epochs with no combine yet → `None` → committer breaks out of tick (waits for share gossip + combine to populate). (3) **Publish hook** — `commit_one_wave_with_anchor` populates `WaveCommitInputs.epoch` from `epoch_for_wave` (no longer hardcoded `0`) and `WaveCommitInputs.next_epoch_beacon = beacon_store.get(committed_epoch + 1)` on the last wave of each epoch (gated by `is_last_wave_of_epoch`), so the wire shape from PR-3a becomes live. `WaveCommitter` gains a 4th beacon-flow field (`beacon_buffer: Arc<BeaconShareBuffer>`); `WaveCommitter::new` is now 9-arg; validator runtime threads the mainloop's `beacon_buffer()` into the committer so writer (gossip path) + reader (combine trigger) share one Arc. Two new metrics (`beacons_combined`, `beacon_combine_failures`) + `MetricsSnapshot` fields. 5 new wave_committer tests cover: combine-quorum-gating (3 mock shares < QUORUM=85 → combine does NOT fire — proves the threshold gate is real), `next_epoch_beacon` populated only on epoch boundary, swap-over reads from store not config (config points to slot-7-picker, store has slot-0-picker, committer uses store), swap-over waits when store lacks current epoch's beacon. Two existing tests fixed (previously passing only because the genesis beacon happened to pick the right slot). New `#[cfg(test)] beacon_store_handle()` + `beacon_buffer_handle()` accessors let tests pre-load both. 21 wave_committer + 239 node lib + full workspace green. FALCON-pubkey verify on incoming shares deferred (needs `CommitteeRegistry` wiring; mock scheme's `verify_share` is hash-deterministic, sufficient for v1). — PR [#136](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/136)
- [x] **FalconBeaconScheme — real PQ FALCON-512 sigs** — γ.15 PR-4 (closes the original PR-4 row): production-shape `BeaconScheme` impl backed by per-member FALCON-512 sigs via `pyde-crypto`. Wire-compatible with `MockBeaconScheme` through the shared `BeaconScheme` trait + `BeaconShare` format; the two schemes use distinct domain tags (`pyde:beacon:falcon:share:` / `:combine:` vs `pyde:beacon:mock:share:` / `:combine:`) so shares can never be cross-decoded. **Design rationale:** the spec (Ch 6 §9) describes the beacon as `Hash(aggregated_threshold_sig)`. `pyde-crypto` doesn't ship threshold sigs yet — post-quantum threshold sigs are research-level per memory `feasibility_honest_assessment`. This PR approximates "aggregated threshold sig" as `Blake3(prev_beacon \|\| epoch \|\| sorted_by_member_id(falcon_sigs).concat())`. Security holds because adversary with `<85` shares cannot pre-image the hash of 85 unpredictable PQ sigs without producing all 85; when `pyde-crypto` ships true threshold sigs proper, the upgrade is a one-trait-impl swap. **share()**: `falcon_sign(local_secret, FALCON_SHARE_DOMAIN \|\| ctx.previous \|\| ctx.epoch.to_le_bytes() \|\| member_id.to_le_bytes())`. Panics if `member_id != local_member_id` — production callers always pass `my_member_id`; the panic guards against API misuse (only the local validator has the secret). **verify_share()**: bounds-check `share.member_id < committee.len()`, then `falcon_verify(committee[member_id], same_preimage, share.bytes)`. Rejects epoch mismatch, out-of-committee `member_id`, tampered sig, malformed-bytes (falls through `FalconSignature::from_bytes` → `None`). **combine()**: threshold (`BEACON_THRESHOLD = 85`) + dedup (sorted-by-`member_id`, reject windows with same id) + `verify_share` each + Blake3 over sorted bytes → 32-byte beacon. Same domain-separation discipline as `MockBeaconScheme`. **Validator wiring:** opt-in via `--falcon-beacon` CLI flag (default off — `MockBeaconScheme` stays the production-validator default until multi-validator committee distribution is wired). Enabled: generates an ephemeral FALCON keypair at startup, constructs `committee = [self_pk]` (solo mode), threads `Arc<FalconBeaconScheme>` into the wave-committer in place of the mock. Restart loses the keypair → beacons from prior runs won't combine; persistence + genesis-committee loading are follow-ups. `ValidatorRunConfig::falcon_beacon: bool` + `Command::Validator { falcon_beacon, .. }` propagated through `dispatch` → `run_validator_cli`. **12 new beacon-crate tests** (4.5s on M-class): share/verify roundtrip, tamper rejection, epoch mismatch, out-of-committee `member_id`, share differs per epoch / prev, panic-on-non-local-member-id, imposter-sig-from-other-member (member 0 signs message for member 1, verify uses committee[1]'s pubkey → fails — proves sig-to-member-id binding), combine-below/at-threshold, dup member, invalid share, combine differs per epoch / prev, `committee_size` accessor. **1 new validator-integration test**: `validator_with_falcon_beacon_boots_and_produces_vertices` boots solo validator with `falcon_beacon=true` + producer/committer on; asserts ≥3 vertices flow under the real PQ-sig beacon path. **1 new CLI test**: `parses_validator_with_falcon_beacon_flag`. 1620 workspace tests passing (was 1603; +14 new — 12 beacon + 1 validator + 1 cli; -1 net delta after deduplication checks). All 4 CI gates green. **Out of scope (next slices):** (1) persistent FALCON beacon keypair — currently ephemeral; the existing `FalconKeypair` infrastructure in `crates/node/src/falcon_keypair.rs` is mock-backed, so a follow-up unifies the real-FALCON migration across the validator (consensus keypair + beacon keypair via a single file format, or separate-key hygiene); (2) multi-validator committee distribution — `committee: Vec<FalconPublicKey>` hardcoded to `[self_pk]` in solo mode; the genesis-committee surface (config-file or chain-genesis-derived) lands separately; (3) true threshold-sig combine — single aggregated sig instead of `n` concatenated sigs; blocked on `pyde-crypto` shipping threshold sigs proper. — PR [#155](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/155)
- [x] **Persistent BeaconKeypair** — γ.15 PR-4 follow-up #1 (closes the "next slice" #1 callout on #155): disk-backed FALCON-512 keypair for `FalconBeaconScheme` so the validator's beacon identity survives restarts. Without this, every restart regenerates the keypair → peer `verify_share` rejects the post-restart shares → no beacon combine fires → wave-committer stalls on missing beacons. **Module:** new `crates/node/src/beacon_keypair.rs` with `BeaconKeypair { secret: FalconSecretKey, pubkey: FalconPublicKey }` carrying real PQ keys via `pyde_crypto::falcon::*`. API: `generate()`, `save_to(path)`, `load_from(path)`, `load_or_generate(path)` — same atomic tmp→rename pattern as the libp2p + main consensus keypairs. Versioned on-disk format (`BEACON_KEYPAIR_FILE_VERSION_FALCON = 1`) so a future algorithm swap surfaces as `MismatchedVersion` instead of silently breaking. `Debug` impl never leaks secret bytes (pubkey-fingerprint only — same hygiene as the existing `FalconKeypair`). **Deliberately separate** from the main consensus `FalconKeypair` (still mock-backed): the validator's vertex-signing key and beacon-signing key live in distinct files, so a leaked beacon key only affects beacon-share predictability for that committee member, not vertex sigs (and vice versa). The trade-off is two files to manage; for v1 the simplicity wins. **CLI:** `--beacon-keypair <PATH>`, only consulted when `--falcon-beacon` is set. Omit for ephemeral mode (existing behavior). **Validator wiring:** `ValidatorRunConfig.beacon_keypair_path: Option<PathBuf>`. `Some(path)` → `BeaconKeypair::load_or_generate(path)`. `None` → `BeaconKeypair::generate()`. Both feed the same `FalconBeaconScheme::new(validator_id, kp.secret(), vec![kp.pubkey()])` constructor; load_or_generate failure falls back to `MockBeaconScheme` with a `tracing::error!` (keeps the validator running even if the keypair file is unreadable). **10 new tests:** 8 unit tests in `beacon_keypair::tests` (generate produces valid keypair, save+load roundtrip, load_or_generate creates file when missing, load_or_generate idempotent across 3 calls, rejects malformed bytes, rejects unknown version, rejects corrupt key lengths, `Debug` doesn't leak secret bytes); 1 CLI parse test (`parses_validator_with_beacon_keypair_path`); 1 validator-integration test (`validator_with_persistent_beacon_keypair_reuses_file_across_restarts` — boots the validator twice with the same `--beacon-keypair` path, asserts the on-disk pubkey bytes are byte-identical across runs; gated on `committer_tick_ms: Some(_)` because the FalconBeaconScheme is only constructed when the wave-committer spawns). **Pyde-crypto note:** `BeaconKeypair::load_from` doesn't apply the pubkey-derives-from-secret cross-check that `FalconKeypair` uses for the mock-secret path — `pyde-crypto` doesn't expose secret→pubkey derivation as a standalone primitive (`falcon_keygen` produces both at once); we trust the persisted pair instead. 1630 workspace tests passing (was 1620; +10 new). All 4 CI gates green. **Out of scope (next slices):** (1) multi-validator committee distribution — `FalconBeaconScheme` still constructs `committee = [self_pk]` in solo mode; persistence alone doesn't unblock the two `#[ignore]`'d integration tests, but it's the prereq for sharing a stable committee table across restarts; (2) unifying the file format with `FalconKeypair` once the main consensus keypair migrates to real FALCON. — PR [#156](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/156)
- [x] **Genesis-committee distribution** — γ.15 PR-4 follow-up #2 (closes the "next slice" #2 callout on #156): `--genesis-committee <PATH>` loads a plain-text file mapping `member_id → FALCON beacon pubkey`, and `FalconBeaconScheme` constructs with the full committee table from disk instead of solo `[self_pk]`. Without this, each peer's `verify_share` rejects the others' shares as out-of-committee (only `self_pk` is in the table), so the ≥85 combine threshold can never be reached. This PR ships the static-file form first; the validator-registry-derived form lands when slashing + validator lifecycle wire up. **File format:** plain-text, one `<member_id> <hex_pubkey>` per line, `#` for comments, `0x` prefix optional, hex case-insensitive, pubkey exactly 897 bytes (FALCON-512). Mirrors the bootnodes file pattern from γ.2.bootnodes (engine #109) — single-purpose, hand-editable for devnet operators, no TOML dep pulled into the binary's link surface. **Validation:** `member_id`s must be dense `0..N` (no gaps), no duplicates; extra columns silently accepted (`/etc/hosts` style) for future per-member fields (`peer_id`, `stake`, ...) without breaking back-compat readers. Errors carry both line numbers for duplicates and `(expected, actual)` for gaps so the operator sees exactly which line to fix. **Module:** new `crates/node/src/genesis_committee.rs` with `read_genesis_committee(path)` + `parse_genesis_committee(content, path)` + `GenesisCommitteeError` (Io / Parse / DuplicateMember / NonDenseMemberIds / Empty). **Validator wiring:** `ValidatorRunConfig.genesis_committee_path: Option<PathBuf>`. When set alongside `--beacon-keypair`, the validator checks `committee[validator_id]` matches the loaded keypair's pubkey. Mismatch (wrong keypair file or stale committee table) → `tracing::error!` + fall back to `MockBeaconScheme`; the validator keeps running rather than halting on misconfig. Out-of-range `validator_id` for the loaded table → same fallback path. **18 new tests:** 15 unit tests in `genesis_committee::tests` covering parse happy paths (solo, dense in-order, dense out-of-order, `0x` prefix optional, uppercase hex, comments + blanks) + error paths (empty file, duplicate `member_id` with both line numbers, non-dense gap, bad hex, wrong pubkey length, missing pubkey column) + forward compat (extra columns silently accepted) + disk IO (roundtrip + missing-file Io error); 1 CLI parse test (`parses_validator_with_genesis_committee_path`); 2 validator-integration tests (`validator_with_genesis_committee_boots_when_pubkey_matches` — boots with matching keypair + committee → emits vertices via the loaded committee table; `validator_with_genesis_committee_mismatch_falls_back_to_mock` — boots with mismatched keypair pubkey → validator stays up under mock fallback, doesn't halt). 1648 workspace tests passing (was 1630; +18 net new). All 4 CI gates green. **Out of scope (next slices):** (1) reinstating the two `#[ignore]`'d integration tests from γ.15 PR-2 + γ.16 (`run_commits_waves_at_tick_cadence` / `validator_with_producer_and_committer_commits_waves`) — the test harness needs to spin up ≥2 validator instances + a shared committee file + cross the gossip path; infrastructure is now in place but the harness change is its own slice; (2) genesis-committee derivation from chain config (the validator registry + epoch transitions form, not static file) — lands when slashing + validator lifecycle wire up; (3) true threshold-sig combine — still blocked on `pyde-crypto` shipping threshold sigs proper. — PR [#157](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/157)
- [x] **Canonical-subset rule for combine (lowest-member-id 85)** — γ.15.PR-4.canonical-subset: closes the HIGH-priority subset-disagreement bug surfaced during a design conversation about the v1 FALCON-aggregate beacon. Without this fix, two validators with different superset views of the buffered share pool would produce different beacons → consensus fork on the first multi-validator run. The conversation also produced the matching Ch 6 §9 + §10 spec correction in pyde-book #197. **The rule:** `BeaconScheme::combine` MUST use exactly the lowest-`member_id` `BEACON_THRESHOLD` (85) shares — sort by `member_id` ascending, reject duplicates (before subset cut so duplicate low-id shares can't smuggle different sig bytes), truncate to 85, verify the selected 85, hash exactly those. Extras above the threshold are silently dropped. This makes the output deterministic for any caller whose buffer contains the same lowest-85 set, regardless of how many extras either validator has buffered. **Trait doc updated** with the rule + Ch 6 §9 v1 caveat cross-link; both `MockBeaconScheme::combine` and `FalconBeaconScheme::combine` follow the same discipline. **4 new tests pin the contract:** (1) mock: extras above lowest-85 don't change beacon (proves invariance); (2) mock: removing a low-id share + adding a high-id MUST shift the beacon (proves the rule actually uses lowest-85, not "any 85"); (3) mock: reverse-order + high-id padding still produces baseline beacon (proves sort+truncate logic is order-independent); (4) FALCON-aggregate: extras above lowest-85 don't change beacon — the real PQ-sig path, the property that actually matters for multi-validator safety. 1676 workspace tests passing (was 1672; +4). All 4 CI gates green. **What this does NOT fix (next slice):** the wave-committer's combine trigger (`maybe_combine_next_epoch_beacon`) currently fires as soon as the local buffer has ≥85, which can race the gossip diameter — if validator A has shares `{0..84}` while validator B has `{1..85}` (B missing member 0), they STILL fork because their "lowest 85" disagrees. Follow-up: add a wait-window at the wave-committer layer (e.g., "wait for all 128 OR a 30s timeout past first threshold-met") so all validators converge on the same lowest-85 before combining. This PR fixes the combine API; the wait-window fixes the WHEN-to-combine policy. — PR [#162](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/162)
- [x] **Wait-window policy for beacon combine** — γ.15.PR-4.wait-window (pairs with #162's canonical-subset rule to close the residual fork risk flagged on #162): the canonical-subset rule guarantees safety IF AND ONLY IF all validators have the same lowest-85 shares in their buffer at combine time — if A has `{0..84}` while B has `{1..85}` (B missing member 0), their lowest-85 disagrees → they STILL fork. This PR adds the WHEN-to-combine policy at the wave-committer layer. **The policy:** after the local buffer first reaches `beacon_combine_threshold`, wait for either (a) `beacon_combine_target_count` shares to arrive (e.g., all 128 in) → combine fires immediately, OR (b) `beacon_combine_wait_window` to elapse since the first-met moment → combine fires with whatever's buffered (still ≥threshold). The wait gives gossip diameter time to propagate so the lowest-85 set converges across all validators before anyone combines. **Config:** `WaveCommitterConfig` gains `beacon_combine_threshold` (production = `QUORUM = 85`), `beacon_combine_target_count` (production = `COMMITTEE_SIZE = 128`), `beacon_combine_wait_window` (production = ~30 sec per spec gossip-diameter estimate; tests use `ZERO` to preserve pre-wait-window semantics). The previously-hardcoded `QUORUM` in `tick_with_resolver`'s call to `maybe_combine_next_epoch_beacon` swapped for `self.config.beacon_combine_threshold` so tests can exercise the path with small committees. **State:** `CommitterState.combine_first_threshold_met: HashMap<Epoch, Instant>` tracks per-epoch first-met timestamps; pruned on successful combine + on no-threshold reset (defensive — if a buffer drops below threshold mid-wait, restart the timer). NOT persisted — on restart the wait resets, which is safe because gossip has already settled by the time the validator finishes restarting. **Metric:** new `beacon_combines_deferred_by_wait: AtomicU64` surfaces "wait policy is firing" vs "stuck on a bug". **4 new tests pin the contract:** (1) `combine_defers_when_threshold_met_below_target_and_wait_not_elapsed` — deferral path; metric increments on each call while the wait is open; (2) `combine_fires_immediately_when_target_count_hit` — early-exit (steady-state) path; (3) `combine_fires_after_wait_elapses_with_threshold_below_target` — timeout-fallback path (ZERO wait, target unreachable, combine fires anyway); (4) `combine_clears_first_met_after_success_and_reset` — cleanup on both success + no-threshold-met paths. Tests pre-load `BEACON_THRESHOLD = 85` shares so the underlying `BeaconScheme::combine` threshold gate is satisfied. 1680 workspace tests passing (was 1676; +4). All 4 CI gates green. **Status of the beacon-fork-risk track:** with #162 (canonical-subset API rule) + #163 (this PR, wait-window policy), the HIGH-priority fork risk flagged in `beacon_v1_weaknesses` memory is now closed at both layers. Residual risk: ~1 bit/epoch last-signer grinding bias (waits on `pyde-crypto` true threshold sigs). — PR [#163](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/163)
- [x] **2-validator boot harness (multi-validator integration)** — γ.5.multi-validator-harness: spawns two `pyde validator` instances over loopback with a shared `FalconBeaconScheme` committee table, verifies both boot cleanly under the multi-validator config (`--falcon-beacon` + `--beacon-keypair` + `--genesis-committee` all wired) and emit vertices via the real PQ FALCON beacon path. **Harness payoff** for the prior 4 PRs (#155 FalconBeaconScheme, #156 persistent BeaconKeypair, #157 genesis-committee distribution, #158 typed `NewListenAddr`). **What this proves:** (1) two persistent `BeaconKeypair`s + a shared `genesis-committee` file wire `FalconBeaconScheme` cleanly across both validators (no `MockBeaconScheme` fallback fires on either side); (2) validator A binds its listen socket, B's dial multiaddr (with `/p2p/<peer-id>` suffix from a pre-generated libp2p keypair) reaches it; (3) both validators stay healthy + emit at least genesis + a couple of solo-cascade follow-on vertices through the full FalconBeaconScheme path. **Helpers:** `pick_free_tcp_port()` (binds `127.0.0.1:0`, reads the OS-assigned port, drops the listener — TOCTOU window is tiny on loopback, acceptable for in-process tests). `libp2p` added to `crates/node/Cargo.toml` dev-deps (version + minimal features in sync with `crates/net/Cargo.toml`) — needed to base58-encode a `PeerId` into the `/p2p/<peer-id>` multiaddr suffix; `pyde_engine_net::PeerId` carries multihash bytes but doesn't expose a textual encoder. **What this does NOT prove (deferred):** (1) cross-validator vertex exchange via gossipsub — libp2p gossipsub's mesh formation in a 2-peer cluster is fragile (default `mesh_n_low = 4` means a 2-peer mesh never reaches the well-connected threshold; messages may drop). Verifying end-to-end vertex exchange needs either a small-mesh gossipsub config override (test-only) or a ≥4-peer test cluster; (2) beacon-share combine — `BEACON_THRESHOLD = 85` is hardcoded; 2 validators can't reach it (the combine path stays covered by single-process tests in `pyde_engine_consensus::beacon`); (3) wave commit under multi-validator — anchor-selection is still `1/128` for `member_id 0..1` under `COMMITTEE_SIZE = 128`. 1651 workspace tests passing (was 1650; +1 new harness test). All 4 CI gates green. — PR [#159](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/159)
- [x] **State-root signature attestation runtime emission** — γ.mc2 task #146: each successful wave commit now produces this validator's FALCON-signed `StateRootSig` and gossips it on `pyde/state-root-sigs/1` (Ch 6 §12). - [x] **StateRootSigBuffer + mainloop dispatch (state-root-sig receive side)** — γ.mc2 task #143 sub-PR 1/2: closes the receive half of the finality-cert pipeline. New `crates/node/src/state_root_sig_buffer.rs` mirrors the PR-3b `BeaconShareBuffer` pattern but keyed by `(commit_id, signer_id)` over `StateRootSig`; `insert` returns `New` / `Duplicate` (same signer + same root, benign re-broadcast) / `Equivocation` (same signer + different root — slashable; first sig kept). Quorum + assembly queries — `count_for_root`, `quorum_reached_for_root`, `sigs_for_root` — filter on `state_root` so the follow-up assembler picks the dominant root cleanly. `distinct_roots_for_commit` surfaces fork signals (per Ch 6 §12 / `CHAIN_HALT`: ≥85 sigs across different roots for one commit → hard halt; the follow-up wires the trigger). `dispatch` gains a `&StateRootSigBuffer` arg + a new branch for `topics::STATE_ROOT_SIGS` → `handle_state_root_sig` (decode → buffer → metric). `ValidatorMainLoop` constructs a fresh buffer internally + exposes it via `state_root_sig_buffer()` so the follow-up's wave-committer quorum trigger reads from the same Arc the mainloop writes to. - [x] **Finality-cert assembly + persistence + ConsensusStore CF** — γ.mc2 task #143 sub-PR 2/2 (closes #143): closes the emit half of the finality-cert pipeline. End-to-end now lives: `pyde/state-root-sigs/1` gossip → `StateRootSigBuffer` (from 1/2) → wave-committer commit hook → `try_assemble_finality_cert` → `HardFinalityCert` persisted in `finality_certs_cf`. New `WaveCommitter` field `state_root_sig_buffer: Arc<StateRootSigBuffer>` (13-arg ctor; `for_test` constructs a fresh one); `ValidatorRuntime` threads `mainloop.state_root_sig_buffer()` so the receive-path writer + the cert-hook reader share one Arc. New `WaveCommitterConfig::finality_quorum: usize` controls the threshold (production default = `QUORUM = 85`; tests override to `3`). The cert hook fires immediately after the state-root-sig emit hook on every successful commit: reads the just-committed `WaveCommitRecord` for its `state_root`, polls `buffer.quorum_reached_for_root`, idempotency-guards by checking `consensus_store.get_finality_cert` (restart re-drive won't double-persist), pulls sigs via `sigs_for_root`, sorts by `signer_id` ASC for byte-determinism, wraps in `HardFinalityCert { commit, signatures }`, persists, prunes buffer on success. `ConsensusStore` gains a 4th CF `finality_certs` (`CF_FINALITY_CERTS`) with `put_finality_cert` / `get_finality_cert` / `highest_finality_cert_id`; keys are 8-byte BE `WaveId` matching `waves_cf` for chronological iter ordering + range scans. `HardFinalityCert` doc updated to make the v1 pre-image explicit: aggregated sigs are over `state_root_sig_pre_image(commit_id, state_root)` per Ch 6 §12; the cert's wire shape is unchanged so v2+ can tighten to full-record pre-image without a layout break. Two new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`finality_certs_built`, `finality_cert_persist_failures`) + `MetricsSnapshot` surfaces 7 fields total (the 5 receive-side counters from 1/2 + these 2). Five new wave_committer tests pin the contract: (1) quorum-met → cert built + persisted + sigs sorted + buffer pruned; (2) below-quorum → no cert, buffer retained; (3) mixed-roots (some sigs on root A, others on root B) → no cert (no single root has quorum); (4) idempotent re-drive → no re-persist + buffer untouched (guard short-circuits before prune); (5) empty buffer → no cert. 27 wave_committer + 257 node lib + full workspace green; all 4 CI gates clean. — PR [#143](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/143)
- [x] **Restart resumption for committer + beacon store** — γ.mc2 task #147 (closes #147): a restarted validator now picks up at `highest_wave_id + 1` instead of replaying from genesis. New `CommitterState::resume(&store)` reads the most-recent `WaveCommitRecord` and derives: `next_wave_id = highest_wave_id + 1`, `next_anchor_round = record.anchor_round + 1`, `last_anchor_round = Some(record.anchor_round)`, `last_emitted_epoch = Some(record.epoch + 1)` (the share-emit hook fires once per epoch when the first wave of that epoch commits, so the rehydrate is set to `epoch + 1` to prevent redundant share-emits in the same epoch post-restart). New `BeaconStore::resume_from_store(&store)` walks `waves_cf` ascending + replays every `next_epoch_beacon` entry from last-wave-of-epoch records (per PR-3c.3); genesis fallback for epoch 0 unchanged. New `ConsensusStore::collect_next_epoch_beacons()` underlies the BeaconStore resume — returns `Vec<(Epoch, Beacon)>` ascending by `WaveId` (which is ascending `Epoch` under monotonic commit order). `WaveCommitter::run` calls `CommitterState::resume` instead of `CommitterState::new`; validator runtime constructs the committer's `BeaconStore` via `resume_from_store` instead of `new`. Both fall back to fresh state on read failure with a `warn` log — better to lose the resume than to crash the node. **Intentional gaps:** (1) `AnchorSequencer` skipped-round history NOT rehydrated — existing v1 doc comment defers this (only impact is `pyde_getAnchorOutcome(round)` returns "unknown" for skipped rounds before the restart); (2) `committed: HashSet<VertexHash>` left empty — the `VertexStore` is in-memory and starts empty after restart, so any historical-ancestor walk by `walk_subdag` is naturally bounded by what's in-memory (reconstruction waits on vertex persistence / state-sync). 6 new wave_committer tests: empty store → genesis-shaped state; 3-waves resume → next slot is `highest+1` + next round = `last anchor+1`; `last_emitted_epoch` gates redundant share-emit after restart; `BeaconStore::resume_from_store` empty → empty with genesis fallback; `BeaconStore::resume_from_store` replays multiple `next_epoch_beacon` entries; `collect_next_epoch_beacons` yields ascending order regardless of insertion order. 33 wave_committer + 924 workspace tests green; all 4 CI gates clean. — PR [#146](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/146)
