- [x] **StateMutator::commit_wave trait reshape for γ↔β handshake** — γ.mc2 task #144 sub-PR 1/2 (interfaces-only): proposes the right `StateMutator::commit_wave` trait surface so β can implement the production orchestrator behind a frozen contract. **Trait change:** old `commit_wave(wave_id, txs: Vec<Tx>) -> WaveCommitRecord` → new `commit_wave(walked_vertices: Vec<Arc<Vertex>>) -> WaveCommitInputs`. The new shape is the right contract: γ produces the BFS sub-DAG ordering via `walk_subdag(anchor)`, β resolves each vertex's `batch_refs` to txs using β's own batch cache, β executes per-tx accumulating `gas_used: u128` + events + receipts, β calls `StateCommitter::commit_with_events` to produce a single atomic state_root + events_root + events_bloom, returns the 7 execution-side `WaveCommitInputs` fields. γ then folds into a `WaveCommitRecord` via `assemble_wave_commit_record(anchor, inputs)`. **Crate moves:** `WaveCommitInputs` moves from `pyde_engine_consensus::wave_commit` → `pyde_engine_types::consensus` so the `interfaces` crate can name it in `StateMutator::commit_wave`'s return type without taking a dep on `consensus` — keeps layer order honest: `types` → `interfaces` → (`consensus` + β); β doesn't depend on `consensus`. `pyde_engine_consensus` re-exports for backwards compat. **Mock + spike updates:** `MockState::commit_wave` matches new shape, returns empty-execution inputs (the mock doesn't crack open `batch_refs`; production β resolves batches + executes per-tx). `DevnetState` (the spike): per-tx execution logic moves to a new public inherent `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs(wave_id, txs) -> WaveCommitInputs`; the trait method returns `NotImplemented` so it's unambiguous that real β implements the resolution + execution end-to-end. Devnet composer pre-resolves batches (it owns the spike's batch cache) + calls the inherent helper directly + patches in the composer-owned `prior_anchor_round` on top of the returned `WaveCommitInputs`. **β audit conclusion** informs this PR: β has the primitives (`StateCommitter.commit_with_events`, full Deploy handler, per-tx Receipt flow with events + return_data) but lacks (1) the orchestrator + (2) the right trait shape + (3) `rollback_wave` persistence; ~4-7 days β-side effort to ship the production impl behind this surface. This is **sub-PR 1/2** for #144 — the 2/2 wires the running wave-committer to call `state.commit_wave(walked_vertices)` once β lands its impl. 930 workspace tests green; all 4 CI gates clean. — PR [#148](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/148)
- [x] **Vertex producer: event-driven on parent quorum** — γ.mc2 task #142 (closes #142): replaces the wall-clock-ticking producer (γ.5 solo-bring-up spike) with the architecturally-correct Mysticeti Ch 6 §4 design — a validator emits round R+1 only when ≥`quorum` parents from round R are in the local DAG. The wall-clock pacing was wrong because: (1) in multi-validator runs, 128 validators all emitted round N+1 in lockstep regardless of whether they'd seen each other's round N — round numbers raced ahead while parent sets stayed sparse; (2) the "2271 vertices in 5s at 250ms tick" observation that prompted the task was a separate runaway bug that the design fix supersedes entirely. **Architecture:** new `VertexStore::insertion_notify() -> Arc<tokio::sync::Notify>` fires once on every successful insert (`New` or `Equivocation`; not `Duplicate`). Uses `notify_one` to stash a permit when no waiter is parked — avoids the missed-wake problem where an insert that lands while the producer is busy emitting would otherwise leave the producer parked forever waiting for the next insert. `VertexProducer::run()` refactored: replaces `tokio::time::interval` with a `select!` over (shutdown, notify, min-tick-floor). On every wake → `parent_quorum_reached()` which checks `select_parents(dag, next_round, usize::MAX).len() >= quorum`. Round 0 has no parent gate (genesis always fires). On condition met → emit + insert + publish + `tokio::task::yield_now()` (cascades through the runtime so shutdown/network/mainloop tasks can run between produces). Sync shutdown check at the top of every loop iteration covers the cascade path where `continue` bypasses the `select!` — without it, lockstep-solo (quorum=1 + zero floor) would never observe a shutdown flip. **Config:** `VertexProducerConfig::quorum: usize` (production = `QUORUM = 85`; tests override to small values for sub-committee scenarios). `tick_interval` repurposed as a min-tick floor against lockstep-solo cascade runaway (default 50ms; was 250ms wall-clock pace). `ValidatorRunConfig::producer_quorum: Option<usize>` + `--producer-quorum` CLI flag — solo/devnet runs pass `Some(1)`, 2-validator devnet uses `Some(2)`, production mainnet uses `None` (= QUORUM = 85). Existing validator tests set `producer_quorum: Some(1)` so solo cascades still advance past genesis. **3 new producer tests pin the contract:** (1) `solo_quorum_one_advances_after_each_insert` — quorum=1 cascade fires ≥5 rounds in 50ms (proves the notify→tick→notify cascade works); (2) `high_quorum_blocks_until_peers_insert_parents` — quorum=3 stalls at genesis until 2 peer round-0 vertices land, then producer wakes via notify + fires round 1 (proves the notify-driven trigger works for multi-validator); (3) `high_quorum_no_peers_produces_only_genesis` — quorum=85 + no peers ever arrive → exactly 1 vertex (genesis) produced (proves the quorum gate is real). 12 producer + 933 workspace tests green; all 4 CI gates clean. — PR [#149](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/149)

- [x] **wasm-exec: drop `pyde::panic` — last legacy alias before otigen's canonical 28-fn surface** — final cleanup of the otigen-engine host fn alignment kicked off by #151. `pyde::panic` was a β.4 PR-4-era plumbing scaffold registered before `pyde::revert` shipped in `host_fns/halt.rs`. The two had identical shape (`(reason_ptr: i32, reason_len: i32) -> !`) and identical semantics (halt + surface a reason string as a trap); the panic-fn body was always a placeholder that returned `Err(wasmtime::Error::msg("contract panic at ptr=X len=Y"))` and never even read the reason bytes from linear memory (real reason-decode landed in `revert`). otigen's canonical `CORE_HOST_FNS` allowlist has `revert` but NOT `panic` → engine drifted at 29 fns instead of the spec's 28. Same class of fix as the `block_height` drop in #151. **Benign drift** (otigen-built contracts wouldn't import `pyde::panic` because otigen's deploy validator would reject it as out-of-allowlist), but worth cleaning up so the engine linker matches the spec exactly. **Changes:** (1) deleted `crates/wasm-exec/src/host_fns/panic.rs` (86 lines + 2 internal `register_panic_*` tests); (2) removed `host_fns::register_panic(&mut linker)?;` from `crates/wasm-exec/src/linker.rs::build_linker`; (3) removed `pub mod panic;` + `pub use panic::register_panic;` from `crates/wasm-exec/src/host_fns/mod.rs`; (4) deleted test `execute_call_surfaces_pyde_panic_host_fn_call_as_trap` in `crates/wasm-exec/src/executor.rs` (the PR-4-era plumbing test that imported `(import "pyde" "panic" ...)` from a WAT contract — semantically replaced by the `revert`-based traps in halt.rs's tests); (5) updated doc comments in `error.rs` (`pyde::panic` → `pyde::revert`), `executor.rs` (two sites: trap-source comment + execute_call's contract-trap list), `host_fns/mod.rs` (replaced "PR-4 ships only panic..." paragraph with "current registered surface: 28 canonical core host fns per HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC §7"), `linker.rs` (build_linker docstring now references the canonical 28-fn surface), and `lib.rs` (retired-PR-4-scaffold note explaining the history). **Verification:** `grep -B 0 -A 2 '"pyde"' crates/wasm-exec/src/host_fns/*.rs | grep -oE '"[a-z_]+"' | sort -u | wc -l` → 28 (was 29). Final 28-fn list matches otigen's `CORE_HOST_FNS` 1:1 — storage 3 (sload/sstore/sdelete) + account 2 (balance/transfer) + context 6 (caller/origin/self_address/wave_id/wave_timestamp/chain_id) + tx 5 (tx_hash/tx_value/tx_gas_remaining/calldata_size/calldata_copy) + events 1 (emit_event) + hashing 3 (hash_blake3/hash_poseidon2/hash_keccak256) + PQ crypto 1 (falcon_verify) + cross-call 3 (cross_call/cross_call_static/delegate_call) + halt 2 (return/revert) + gas 1 (consume_gas) + beacon 1 (beacon_get). - [x] **Wave-committer ↔ DevnetState wiring: production validator executes committed waves end-to-end** — γ.mc2 task #144 sub-PR 2/2 (closes #144 entirely). Closes the γ↔β trait handshake started in #144 sub-PR 1/2 (engine #148, landed via the integration merge #150). The production `pyde validator` binary's wave-committer now invokes a real state executor on every commit — resolving walked vertices → txs end-to-end via the shared `BatchCache` + `ConsensusStore.txs_cf` — instead of constructing empty placeholder `WaveCommitInputs`. This is the **v1-spike-level integration**: `DevnetState` (β's MC-2.1 work, inherited via the integration merge) runs the actual transfer/fee/nonce logic. When β's wasm-exec orchestrator (`StateStore` production impl) ships post-MC-2, the wiring swap is a one-line change in `ValidatorRuntime` (replace the `Arc<DevnetState>` construction with the real `Arc<StateStore>` once it implements `commit_walked_subdag` or the production-shaped equivalent). **Per persistent memory `wasm_exec_atomic_relaxed_assumes_single_threaded`**: this is safe because the wave-committer's tick remains single-threaded per Mysticeti spec (one wave at a time); a γ-side integrator who parallelizes per-tx execution within a wave MUST add an outer mutex around state access. **Changes:** `crates/node/src/devnet/state.rs` — `DevnetState` gains two optional fields (`batch_cache: Option<Arc<BatchCache>>` + `consensus_store: Option<Arc<ConsensusStore>>`) plus paired constructor `new_with_caches(fee_config, batch_cache, consensus_store)`; existing `new(fee_config)` keeps Option as `None` (preserves devnet composer + existing-test behavior). New inherent method `commit_walked_subdag(wave_id, walked_vertices: &[Arc<Vertex>]) -> Result<WaveCommitInputs, InterfaceError>`: returns `NotImplemented` if caches aren't wired (composer path stays as-is — pre-resolves via `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs`); otherwise for each vertex iterates `batch_refs` → looks up bytes in `BatchCache` → borsh-decodes the `Batch` → walks `batch.tx_hashes` → looks up each `Tx` in `consensus_store.txs_cf` → delegates the resolved `Vec<Tx>` to the existing `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs`. Missing batches (gossip race), missing txs (txs_cf miss), and borsh decode failures are skipped silently + logged at `warn` — the wave commits what's resolvable, matching the network's eventual-consistency model. `crates/node/src/runtime.rs` — `ValidatorRuntime` gains `state: Arc<DevnetState>` constructed via `new_with_caches` with the runtime's shared `BatchCache` + `ConsensusStore`. `crates/node/src/wave_committer.rs` — `WaveCommitter` gains `state: Arc<DevnetState>` (12-arg ctor; existing arg order preserved). `for_test` default state constructs via `DevnetState::new` (no caches → NotImplemented fallback exercised by existing tests, preserving pre-#144 behavior). `commit_one_wave_with_anchor` swaps the placeholder `WaveCommitInputs` construction for `state.commit_walked_subdag(wave_id, &walked)`: on `Ok(inputs)` use the state's execution-derived fields (state_root, events_root, events_bloom, events_count, gas_used, included_txs), then patch composer-owned consensus-side fields on top (prior_anchor_round, epoch, next_epoch_beacon); on `Err(NotImplemented)` fall back to empty inputs (legacy path); on `Err(Storage|Internal)` log + fall back to empty inputs (the wave still commits — lossy but doesn't halt the chain). `crates/node/src/validator.rs` — production validator threads `runtime.state.clone()` into the wave-committer ctor. **4 new resolution tests in `devnet/state.rs` pin the contract:** (1) `commit_walked_subdag_returns_not_implemented_when_caches_missing` — unwired state → NotImplemented (proves composer path stays valid); (2) `commit_walked_subdag_resolves_batches_and_executes_txs_end_to_end` — pre-loaded batch (in BatchCache) + tx (in txs_cf) → resolved + executed → non-EMPTY state_root, gas_used == 21000, included_txs == [tx_hash] (proves the full resolution chain works); (3) `commit_walked_subdag_skips_missing_batch_in_cache` — vertex refs unknown batch hash → skipped silently, wave commits empty (proves graceful degradation under gossip races); (4) `commit_walked_subdag_skips_tx_missing_from_consensus_store` — batch resolves but tx hash absent from txs_cf → skipped silently (proves txs_cf miss handling). 1600 workspace tests passing (was 1596; +4 new). All 4 CI gates green. **Out of scope (next slice):** the production producer doesn't yet fill vertex `batch_refs` (mempool drain → Batch construction → BatchCache put → vertex batch_refs). Until that lands, live `pyde validator` runs still produce empty waves on the wire — but the spine is now wired + testable, and the moment producer-side ships, real state changes flow end-to-end without further wave-committer changes. — PR [#153](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/153)
- [x] **Producer ↔ mempool ↔ batch wiring: live waves now carry real txs** — γ.5.producer-wiring. Closes the "next slice" callout from #153 (engine roadmap line 332): the production `VertexProducer` now drains the live `PydeMempoolView` into a `Batch` on every tick, persists each tx to `consensus_store.txs_cf` keyed by canonical `pyde_engine_tx::tx_hash` (the spec-correct Poseidon2-based hash per Ch 11 §11.6), borsh-encodes the `Batch` and caches it under `batch_hash = blake3(borsh(tx_hashes) ++ borsh(encryption_metadata))` in the shared `BatchCache`, and embeds `[batch_hash]` in the vertex's `batch_refs`. Empty mempool → empty `batch_refs` (round still advances). The resolution chain wired in #153 (`DevnetState::commit_walked_subdag` → `BatchCache.get` → `borsh::from_slice<Batch>` → `batch.tx_hashes` → `consensus_store.get_tx`) now sees real batches end-to-end. **Mainloop side**: gossiped txs (already persisted to `txs_cf` per γ.5.mempool-persistence) now ALSO admit into `PydeMempoolView::insert` via a fire-and-forget `tokio::spawn`, mirroring the state-root-sig + beacon-share emit pattern from #138. This runs the full validation pipeline (FALCON sig + balance + nonce window + chain_id + structural per PR [#129](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/129)) before the tx becomes drainable. `ValidatorRuntime` constructs the mempool over the same `Arc<DevnetState>` used as `StateView` so balance/nonce/auth-keys lookups stay coherent. **`BatchPipeline` design**: optional wiring attached via `VertexProducer::with_batch_pipeline(...)` so the producer remains usable in tests / solo bring-up without dragging in mempool + RocksDB. The `mempool` field is typed `Arc<dyn MempoolView>` so unit tests use the no-validation `MockMempool` while production wires the same concrete `PydeMempoolView` the mainloop admits txs into. Per-tick budget on serialized-tx bytes defaults to `BATCH_MAX_BYTES = 4 MB` per Mysticeti Ch 6 §2. Tx-persist failures (txs_cf put error) degrade gracefully — log + drop the affected tx; the wave-committer's existing `consensus_store.get_tx(...) → None` branch handles the resulting batch_ref → tx miss without aborting the wave. **3 new producer tests**: (1) `assemble_batch_refs_empty_mempool_returns_empty` — empty drain → empty refs (proves the no-tx path stays clean); (2) `assemble_batch_refs_persists_txs_caches_batch_and_returns_hash` — admit-drain-persist-cache cycle yields a `Batch` decodable from `BatchCache` with `tx_hashes = [h]` + `encryption_metadata = None`, and the tx is recoverable from `consensus_store.get_tx(&h)` (proves the full resolution chain); (3) `run_with_pipeline_emits_vertex_with_batch_refs` — live run with one admitted tx publishes a first vertex with one `batch_ref` then empty-`batch_refs` vertices after (proves the producer emits real waves on the wire). **3 new metrics**: `producer_batches_assembled` (non-empty batches emitted), `producer_txs_packed` (cumulative txs across batches), `producer_tx_persist_failures` (drained txs that failed `put_tx`; degrades gracefully). 1603 workspace tests passing (was 1600; +3 new). All 4 CI gates green. **Out of scope (next slice)**: priority-fee tx ordering (HARD-excluded per memory `hard_excluded_v1_features`); the per-batch encryption envelope (`encryption_metadata`) — v1 ships plaintext-only, threshold-decryption ceremony comes with the DKG production rollout (γ.15 PR-4). — PR [#154](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/154)
- [x] **wasm-exec: align `caller` / `origin` / `self_address` to HOST_FN_ABI §7.3 `-> i32`** — surfaced by otigen Phase 1 integration brief A1. The three address-shaped context fns were registered as `(i32) -> ()`; per HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC §7.3 (frozen at v1 mainnet per memory `host-fn-abi-spec-locked.md`) each returns `i32` (always `0` for success). The mismatch caused every otigen-built contract to fail at instantiate-time with `incompatible import type for pyde::self_address`. Each closure now returns `Ok(0)` after the existing memory write; module-level doc + four inline WAT test fixtures pick up `(result i32)` + a trailing `drop`. Unblocks `engine_runner::tests::counter_rust_increments_via_real_engine_wasm_exec` which was `#[ignore]`'d pending this alignment. Surfaced via the otigen-test integration that consumes engine's `build_linker` directly — Phase 1's whole point being "consume engine wasm-exec so spec drift surfaces at integration, not at mainnet". — PR [#167](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/167)
- [x] **wasm-exec: bump wasmtime 26 → 36 (+ matching wasmparser 0.236)** — surfaced by otigen Phase 1 integration brief A2: otigen had to downgrade to wasmtime 26 to consume engine's `build_linker` directly. Engine workspace now on `wasmtime = "36"` + `wasmparser = "0.236"`. Production binary now carries one wasmparser (was two during the bump window). Migration: `Config::static_memory_maximum_size` renamed to `Config::memory_reservation` (wasmtime 36 unified static/dynamic memory configuration; same per-slot virtual-reservation cap semantic — still caps the pool's per-instance max at `POOL_MAX_MEMORY_SIZE` so the kernel doesn't reject the mmap). Pool allocator API (`total_core_instances`, `total_memories`, `total_tables`, `max_memory_size`, `linear_memory_keep_resident`, `table_keep_resident`) unchanged. - [x] **wasm-exec: `pyde.abi` selector dispatch + attribute pre-checks** — implements HOST_FN_ABI §3.5.2 per-call dispatch flow end-to-end. Engine moves from "void-void single entry-point" demo shape to canonical spec contract dispatch. New `WasmExecutor::execute_contract_call` is the canonical Standard tx entry point: looks up the cached `ContractAbi`, resolves the entry point via `dispatch.rs::resolve` (selector → fallback → receive → `ERR_INVALID_FUNCTION_NAME`), applies attribute pre-checks before invoking the WASM body — `CONSTRUCTOR` post-deploy lockout → `ERR_CONSTRUCTOR_LOCKOUT`; `PAYABLE` missing on non-zero `tx.value` → `ERR_VALUE_TRANSFER_NOT_PAYABLE`; `VIEW` → flips `HostContext::view_mode = true` so mutating host fns (`sstore`, `sdelete`, `transfer`, `emit_event`) trap with `ERR_FORBIDDEN` per §3.7 Layer 3 enforcement. New `dispatch.rs` module hosts the pure resolution logic (10 unit tests covering every branch). `ModuleCache` extended per §3.6 to store the parsed `ContractAbi` alongside the compiled module — `compile_and_cache` attempts `extract_pyde_abi` after validation; success stores `Some(Arc<ContractAbi>)`, failure stores `None` (graceful for raw-WASM legacy fixtures). New `ModuleCache::get_with_abi` returns `(Module, Arc<ContractAbi>)` for the dispatch path; new `ExecutorError::AbiMissing` is the graceful-signal variant for raw-WASM fixtures that should keep using the un-dispatched `execute_call` path. 22 new tests (10 dispatch resolution unit + 11 executor-level dispatch integration + 1 end-to-end view-mode runtime enforcement where a `VIEW` fn calling `sstore` traps with the forbidden error). All 201 pre-existing wasm-exec tests remain green via the un-dispatched `execute_call` path. Unblocks otigen Phase 3 multi-entry contracts dispatched by selector + attribute-enforced at runtime. Surfaced by otigen Phase 1 integration brief A5. — PR [#171](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/171)

- [x] Equivocation detection + evidence collection → γ.4 Slashing — `VertexStore::insert` already detected equivocations and returned `InsertOutcome::Equivocation { prior_at_slot }`; this PR adds the event-channel side. New `EquivocationDetected` struct (member_id, round, new_hash, full new_vertex cloned in, prior_at_slot insertion-order list) emitted via an optional `tokio::sync::mpsc::UnboundedSender` attached through `set_equivocation_sink` / `clear_equivocation_sink`. Default = no sink (existing callers unaffected). Receiver-drop is silently swallowed — equivocation is *stored* regardless; only the notification is lost. Completes the consensus-side half of the loop opened by γ.5.equivocation (the node-side `EquivocationDetector::handle_equivocation` is already wired); a follow-up PR adds the main-loop drain task once a verifier + DKG + epoch + stake oracle is available. — PR [#85](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/85)

- [x] Layered peer discovery — **mDNS LAN layer shipped (dev-only)**: libp2p `mdns` feature + `mdns::tokio::Behaviour` composed into `PydeBehaviour.mdns: Toggle<_>` (Toggle keeps the behaviour opt-in without forking the swarm builder). `enable_mdns: bool` threaded through `Network::new` → `NetworkRunner::from_keypair` → `ValidatorRuntimeConfig` → `ValidatorRunConfig` → CLI; surfaced as `pyde validator --enable-mdns` (default off — mDNS broadcasts validator presence to the LAN and is unsafe on a public node). - [x] **Typed `NewListenAddr` event (closes test-flake)** — γ.net.NewListenAddr: replace the string-parser in `two_networks_exchange_gossipsub_message` with a typed `NetworkEvent::NewListenAddr { addr: Multiaddr }` variant. The prior test regex-matched `SwarmEvent::NewListenAddr`'s `Debug` repr, so it broke whenever libp2p added or renamed inner fields (`listener_id`, `address`, ...); the typed variant is structural — no parsing. **Side benefit:** the typed event is the exact surface a future multi-validator integration harness needs for port discovery (bind `/tcp/0`, drain events until `NewListenAddr` fires, hand the resolved `Multiaddr` to the peer's `--dial` config — same pattern the soak-test + chaos-test infrastructure will lean on per memory `performance_harness`). **Changes:** new `NetworkEvent::NewListenAddr` variant; `Network::handle_event` intercepts `SwarmEvent::NewListenAddr` explicitly instead of falling through to the `Debug`-formatted `Other` variant; mainloop dispatch funnels the new variant into the existing `passthrough_events` metric (validators never need to handle their own listen addrs at the consensus layer); `two_networks_exchange_gossipsub_message` rewritten to use the typed variant + **`#[ignore]` removed** (it was only ignored because the parser was flaky, not because it was slow) — now runs in CI; new `new_listen_addr_event_carries_resolved_address` test pins the typed surface (`/ip4/127.0.0.1/tcp/<NON-ZERO>`). 1650 workspace tests passing (was 1648; +2: the un-ignored test runs now + the new pin). All 4 CI gates green. — PR [#158](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/158)

Caller pre-validates `share_pubkey` against chain state. **Safety-offense evidence catalog is now complete.** — PR [#53](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/53)
- [x] Evidence-to-escrow pipeline: `process_evidence(evidence, stake, verifier, slasher, escrow) → ProcessOutcome` — verify → slash → escrow in one call, plus convenience builders for the three verified Safety payloads + `preview_slash` for RPC dry-runs. Resolution of `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` → Vertex stays in node binary (γ.5) — slashing doesn't observe consensus state directly. — PR [#32](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/32)
- [x] **BadStateRootSignature detector → slashing pipeline** — γ.slashing.bad-state-root-sig: closes the wire that `StateRootSigBuffer`'s `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` had set up but nothing was consuming. State-root-sig double-signs now flow into the slashing pipeline the same way vertex equivocations do via γ.mc2 #145. **Buffer surface change:** `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` upgraded from a unit variant → `{ prior: StateRootSig, new: StateRootSig }` so consumers can build evidence directly from the outcome. New `equivocation_sink: RwLock<Option<UnboundedSender<...>>>` + `set_equivocation_sink` / `clear_equivocation_sink` mirroring `VertexStore::set_equivocation_sink`. Sink emits `StateRootSigEquivocationDetected { signer_id, commit_id, prior, new }`. Receiver-drop silently swallowed (send-or-drop) so a slow consumer can't hold up subsequent inserts. **New `BadStateRootSigConsumer` (mirrors `EquivocationConsumer`):** drains the buffer's equivocation channel, builds evidence via `pyde_engine_slashing::build_bad_state_root_sig_evidence`, runs through `process_evidence` → `Slasher` + `Escrow`, persists slasher + escrow snapshots after each successful slash via `with_persistence` (γ.slashing.persistence + escrow-persistence pattern from #160 + #161). v1 stubs identical to the `EquivocationConsumer`: `AcceptingVerifier`, `MockDkg`, `DEFAULT_EPOCH`, `DEFAULT_STAKE` — the buffer's own slot-collision detection is the meaningful gate at v1; tightening lands with the committee registry. **Validator wiring:** spawns a new `bsrs_task` alongside the equivocation consumer + joins on shutdown. Two new metrics: `bad_state_root_sig_consumer_processed` + `bad_state_root_sig_consumer_rejected`. **7 new tests:** 3 buffer (sink fires on equivocation / sink swallows receiver-drop / no-sink-attached still surfaces outcome to caller); 4 consumer (happy-path slash / matching-roots rejection via `verify_evidence`'s defensive check / run-drains-then-exits / run-exits-on-shutdown). 1687 workspace tests passing (was 1680; +7). All 4 CI gates green. **Detector status update:** of the 9 offenses in the catalog, 2 now have running detectors in the validator binary — `Equivocation` (vertex double-sign, #145) + `BadStateRootSignature` (this PR). The remaining 7 (`BadAnchorAttestation`, `InvalidVertexStructure`, `BadDecryptionShare`, `DkgParticipationFailure`, `DecryptionShareWithholding`, `ExtendedDowntime`, `BadBatchAttestation`) need detectors using the same `with_persistence`-style pattern; several depend on subsystems that haven't shipped yet (DKG production protocol, threshold-decryption ceremony, downtime tracking). — PR [#164](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/164)
- [x] **InvalidVertexStructure detector → slashing pipeline** — γ.slashing.invalid-vertex-structure: 3rd of 9 catalog offenses to get a running detector. Vertices that gossip in with `DuplicateBatchRefs` or `InsufficientParentQuorum` (the two members of `StructuralViolation`'s slashable subset) are now dropped from the local DAG and the producer is slashed through the same pipeline as `Equivocation` (γ.mc2 #145) + `BadStateRootSignature` (γ.slashing #164). **Consensus crate:** new `detect_slashable_structural_violation(vertex, quorum) -> Option<ConsensusError>` — pure check, no DAG / verifier / committee table needed; returns the first slashable violation found. Cheap enough for the receive-path hot loop. **Node crate:** new `crates/node/src/invalid_vertex_structure_consumer.rs` mirrors `EquivocationConsumer` + `BadStateRootSigConsumer` pattern. Drains detection events → `build_invalid_vertex_structure_evidence` → `process_evidence` → slasher + escrow → snapshot persistence. Same v1 stubs as peer consumers (`AcceptingVerifier`, `MockDkg`, default epoch + stake). New `InvalidVertexStructureDetected { accused, vertex, code, reporter }` event type — carries the bad vertex itself in the payload so the consumer can build evidence without going back to the (now-empty) store. **Mainloop wiring:** `ValidatorMainLoop` gains optional `set_invalid_vertex_structure_sink` (mirrors `VertexStore::set_equivocation_sink` discipline — drop-on-no-receiver, fire-and-forget). `dispatch` gains a 9th param threading the sink through. `handle_vertex_bytes` calls `detect_slashable_structural_violation` BEFORE insert; on violation → emit event + drop vertex (no insert). **Detection is gated on the sink being attached** — tests that pass `None` skip the check, preserving pre-slashing semantics for the 30+ existing dispatch tests that build vertices without 85 parents. **Validator binary:** constructs the channel BEFORE the mainloop task spawns so the first dispatch sees `Some(tx)`. Joins the new consumer on shutdown alongside the other consumers. **3 new metrics:** `invalid_vertex_structure_detected` (gossiped vertices dropped by the pre-check) + `invalid_vertex_structure_consumer_processed` + `invalid_vertex_structure_consumer_rejected`. **12 new tests:** 5 detector helper (clean / duplicate / insufficient parents / genesis-no-parent-check / duplicate-takes-precedence); 5 consumer (happy-path dup-batch-refs / happy-path insufficient parents / clean-vertex rejected by `verify_evidence`'s defensive check / run drains-and-exits / run exits on shutdown); 2 mainloop (dup-batch-refs gets dropped + routed to sink / no-sink-attached skips detection entirely). 1699 workspace tests passing (was 1687; +12). All 4 CI gates green. **Detector status update:** 3/9 catalog offenses have running detectors now — `Equivocation` (#145) + `BadStateRootSignature` (#164) + `InvalidVertexStructure` (this PR, #165). Remaining 6 mostly block on subsystems not yet shipped (DKG production protocol, threshold-decryption ceremony, downtime tracking, β's batch validation). `BadAnchorAttestation` is the only one whose dependencies are already in tree — consensus subsystem exists, detector wire pending. — PR [#165](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/165)
- [x] **BadAnchorAttestation detector → slashing pipeline** — γ.slashing.bad-anchor-attestation: 4th of 9 catalog offenses to wire a running detector. New `crates/node/src/anchor_attestation_buffer.rs` tracks per-round `prev_anchor_attestation` claims keyed by `(round, attested_anchor)`. When some bucket crosses QUORUM (= 85 distinct members) it locks the majority for that round; every other attester is flagged as a slashable minority and emitted on a detection sink via `BadAnchorAttestationDetected { accused, disputed, honest_majority }` (the full majority vertices are snapshotted so the consumer can build evidence without re-querying any store). The buffer also handles late-arriving minorities (post-`MajorityReached`) via `InsertOutcome::LateMinorityFlagged`. New `BadAnchorAttestationConsumer` mirrors the IVS/BadStateRootSig consumer pattern: drains the channel, calls the new `build_bad_anchor_attestation_evidence` slashing-crate builder, runs `process_evidence`, persists slasher + escrow snapshots to RocksDB. Unlike `InvalidVertexStructure`, the disputed vertex is structurally well-formed (dispute is purely about its attestation content, not its parent quorum or batch refs), so it stays in the local DAG — the wave-committer can still use it; only the producer is slashed. Wired into `ValidatorMainLoop` alongside the IVS sink; spawned in the validator binary alongside the equivocation / bad-state-root-sig / invalid-vertex-structure consumers. Remaining 5 of 9 offenses (BadDecryptionShare, DkgParticipationFailure, DecryptionShareWithholding, ExtendedDowntime, BadBatchAttestation) block on subsystems not yet shipped (DKG production protocol, threshold-decryption ceremony, downtime tracking, β batch validation). — PR [#166](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/166)
- [x] **Slasher snapshot to RocksDB** — γ.slashing.persistence: closes the slasher half of the roadmap "Persistence: Slasher + Escrow to RocksDB" line. Validators now resume their offense log + jail map across restarts instead of losing slashing state on every node bounce. **Design:** new `SlasherSnapshot { offenses: Vec<((u64, u32), Vec<Offense>)>, jail_until: Vec<(u32, u64)> }` borsh-serialisable + sorted by `(epoch, accused)` / `accused` ascending so byte output is deterministic regardless of HashMap iteration order. New `Slasher::snapshot()` + `Slasher::restore(snap)` inverses. **Layout:** `ConsensusStore` gains `CF_SLASHER` with `SLASHER_SNAPSHOT_KEY = b"snapshot"` — v1 has rare slashing events so "rewrite whole snapshot on every record" is negligible; future versions can shard by epoch if needed. New `ConsensusStore::put_slasher_snapshot` / `get_slasher_snapshot`. **Runtime resume:** `ValidatorRuntime::build()` calls `get_slasher_snapshot()` at startup and `Slasher::restore` if `Some`; falls back to fresh `Slasher` with a `warn` log on read failure (same "better to lose the resume than crash the node" discipline as `BeaconStore::resume_from_store` from γ.mc2 #147). **Consumer wiring:** new `EquivocationConsumer::with_persistence(consensus_store)` builder. On `Ok(_)` from the detector, snapshot is taken + put to disk. Persist failure logs at `error` + bumps new `slasher_persistence_failures` metric; in-memory state already reflects the slash so the failure is bounded by "one event lost on subsequent crash". 12 new tests: 6 slasher (empty / offense-log roundtrip / jail_until roundtrip / byte-determinism / borsh roundtrip / clear_jail propagates), 3 consensus_store (empty / put+get / overwrite), 1 runtime (restart resume), 2 consumer (with/without persistence). 1663 workspace tests passing (was 1651; +12). All 4 CI gates green. **Out of scope (next slice):** Escrow persistence (in-flight slash records during dispute window) — same snapshot pattern fits cleanly; lands separately. Slasher writes from non-equivocation paths (BadStateRootSignature, BadAnchorAttestation, DecryptionShareWithholding, ExtendedDowntime, etc.) — each needs a similar `with_persistence`-style attachment when those detectors land. — PR [#160](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/160)
- [x] **Escrow snapshot to RocksDB** — γ.slashing.escrow-persistence (closes the second half of the original "Persistence: Slasher + Escrow to RocksDB" line; pairs with #160): same snapshot pattern as the slasher, now for the dispute-window escrow. Validators resume in-flight slash records across restarts so a crash during the dispute window doesn't double-enqueue or lose matured payouts. **Slashing crate:** `SlashBreakdown` + `EscrowStatus` + `EscrowEntry` gain `BorshSerialize`/`BorshDeserialize` derives; new `EscrowSnapshot { dispute_window_epochs, next_id, entries }` is borsh-serialisable + sorted by `EscrowId` for deterministic bytes; `Escrow::snapshot()` / `Escrow::restore(snap)` inverses. **Critical:** `Escrow::restore` preserves `dispute_window_epochs` from the snapshot (NOT a separate constructor arg) so a future refactor can't silently shift pending entries' effective maturity — that would be a data-integrity hazard worse than crashing. **Node crate:** `ConsensusStore` gains `CF_ESCROW` + `put_escrow_snapshot` / `get_escrow_snapshot` under `ESCROW_SNAPSHOT_KEY` single-key layout. `ValidatorRuntime::build()` calls `get_escrow_snapshot` at startup; `Escrow::restore` if `Some`, `Escrow::new(config.dispute_window_epochs)` otherwise. `EquivocationConsumer::new` takes `escrow: Arc<Escrow>` as new param; on `Ok(_)` from the detector (after `process_evidence` enqueued the entry), BOTH slasher snapshot AND escrow snapshot persist. New `escrow_persistence_failures` metric for the latter. 9 new tests: 6 escrow snapshot/restore (empty / entries preserved with Pending+Voided status retained / next_id continuity for fresh enqueue / byte-determinism / borsh roundtrip / dispute_window preserved); 2 consensus_store (empty store → None / put+get roundtrip); 1 runtime restart-resume test that asserts dispute_window_epochs is preserved from the snapshot. Existing slasher persistence test extended to also assert the escrow snapshot is persisted on the same dispatch. 1672 workspace tests passing (was 1663; +9). All 4 CI gates green. **Closes** the original roadmap line: with #160 (Slasher half) + #161 (Escrow half), validators now resume the full slashing state machine across restarts end-to-end. — PR [#161](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/161)
- [x] Reward distribution math: `distribute_rewards(pool, entries)` pure function (pool × stake × uptime, sum-invariant bit-exact, u128-overflow-safe fallback, 6-decimal `UPTIME_PRECISION`) — PR [#31](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/31)
- [ ] Reward distribution wiring: `UptimeTracker` from consensus attestation events + `RewardPool` epoch-accumulator (depends on γ.1 attestation surface)

#### γ.5 `node` crate `[SEQ within γ] → γ.1 + γ.2 + γ.4` — owned by γ; integration point
- [x] `EquivocationDetector` — node-level wiring between consensus's `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` and slashing's `process_evidence`. Composes Arc'd `VertexStore` + `Slasher` + `Escrow`; `handle_equivocation` looks up the prior, builds Evidence, runs the slash pipeline. Closes the resolution side noted in slashing.12. — PR [#56](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/56)
- [x] `ValidatorRuntime` composition: holds disk-backed libp2p `Keypair` + Arc'd `VertexStore` + `Slasher` + `Escrow` + `ValidatorRegistry` + `EquivocationDetector` + `NetworkHandle`. `ValidatorRuntime::build(config)` returns `{ runtime, network_runner, network_events }` so caller controls tokio spawn; main loop consumes the event stream + uses the runtime. Foundation for the validator binary. — PR [#58](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/58)
- [x] `ConsensusVertexProvider` + `BatchCache` + `BatchCacheProvider`: adapters that satisfy `pyde_engine_net::VertexProvider` / `BatchProvider` from `Arc<VertexStore>` + an in-memory `Arc<BatchCache>`. `ValidatorRuntime::build` wires real providers through `NetworkProviders` instead of the `new_null` placeholder; inbound vertex-fetch / batch-fetch requests now answer out of the runtime's authoritative storage. — PR [#60](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/60)
- [x] `ValidatorMainLoop` + `dispatch()` + `MainLoopMetrics`: long-running tokio task that drains `NetworkEventStream` into the runtime's `VertexStore` + `BatchCache`. Routes vertices (gossip + fetch responses → `VertexStore::insert`, counting `New` / `Duplicate` / `Equivocation`) and batches (gossip → cache by decoded hash; fetch response → cache by requested hash). 10 atomic counters surfaced via `MainLoopMetrics`. `tokio::select!` biased on a `watch::Receiver<bool>` shutdown signal. `NetworkEventStream::channel()` constructor added so tests drive the loop without a real libp2p swarm. Equivocation evidence dispatch deferred to follow-up (needs committee/DKG/stake oracle). — PR [#63](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/63)
- [x] `VertexProducer` solo-validator task — the chain's heartbeat. tokio task that ticks at a configurable interval (default 250 ms, `--producer-tick-ms <MS>`; `0`/omit = disabled), builds a fresh signed `Vertex` for the local validator's slot via `pyde_engine_consensus::VertexBuilder` + `select_parents`, FALCON-signs via the runtime's `FalconKeypair`, inserts into local `VertexStore`, publishes on `pyde/vertices/1`. `tokio::interval` with `MissedTickBehavior::Skip` so paused validators don't burst; `tokio::select!` biased on shutdown. Publish failures (no peers) bump a counter and the task keeps ticking. 2 new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`vertices_produced`, `vertex_publish_failures`). End-to-end verified: `pyde validator --producer-tick-ms 100 …` produces ~10 vertices/sec observable via `pyde_getMetrics`. Anchor selection + wave-commit walking + threshold decryption + DKG + committee rotation all land in follow-ups. — PR [#93](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/93)
- [x] `WaveCommitter` task — **the chain commits + replicates**. tokio task that ticks at a configurable interval (default 125 ms, `--committer-tick-ms <MS>`; `0`/omit = disabled), scans the local `VertexStore` for new anchor rounds, walks the causal sub-DAG via `pyde_engine_consensus::walk_subdag`, calls `assemble_wave_commit_record` with empty β-side inputs (state_root, events, included_txs all empty for now — `StateMutator::commit_wave` populates these once β.3 ships), and persists via `consensus_store.put_wave`. `pick_anchor` selects the deterministic anchor for the round — among honest slots (single vertex per `(round, member_id)`), the lowest `member_id` wins; equivocating slots are skipped. `committed: HashSet<VertexHash>` excludes prior-wave ancestors from each new walk; `prior_anchor_round` threads through correctly. Transient missing-anchor (peer vertex still propagating) waits for the next tick without advancing state; hard failures (assemble overflow, store IO) advance to avoid spinning. 3 new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`wave_commit_attempts`, `waves_committed`, `wave_commit_failures`). End-to-end verified solo (PR [#97](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/97)): `pyde validator --producer-tick-ms 100 --committer-tick-ms 50` produced 13 vertices + committed 12 waves in 2s with 0 failures; `pyde_getWave(0..N)` returns real `WaveCommitRecord`s. Multi-validator (PR [#100](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/100)): `--validator-id <N>` (default 0; range `[0, 128)` enforced) threads through to `VertexProducerConfig::member_id`; two `pyde validator` instances with distinct ids that dial each other share a DAG and commit identical wave records (deterministic anchor selection makes both sides agree without VRF). VRF anchor selection wired in γ.15 PR-2 (PR [#112](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/112)); N/3+1 quorum vote threshold + skip rules wired in γ.16 (PR [#120](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/120)); sentry pattern still pending.
- [x] `pyde` binary — validator mode shipped: `pyde validator --keypair <path> [--listen <addr>]… [--dial <addr>]… [--dispute-window-epochs N]` builds a `ValidatorRuntime`, spawns the libp2p runner + `ValidatorMainLoop`, waits for Ctrl+C, drains, exits. `run_validator(config, shutdown: F)` takes the shutdown future as a parameter so tests drive the lifecycle without installing a real signal handler. Prints a stable post-shutdown summary (PeerId hex, listen/dial addrs, all 10 mainloop counters). Full-node + light-client modes wire in later. — PR [#67](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/67)
- [x] **`pyde devnet` long-running mode + prefunded accounts + banner** — surfaced by otigen Phase 1 integration brief A4: foundation slice of the Anvil-shaped single-process devnet that contract authors hardcode against. `pyde devnet` (without `--smoke`) now launches a long-running single-validator loop. **Deterministic seed**: `devnet_secret(i) = Blake3("pyde-devnet-v1/" || i.to_le_bytes())` — same 10 addresses + secrets every run on every machine. The `v1` prefix locks the algorithm for v1 mainnet (rotating requires a deliberate `v2` constant). **Genesis prefund**: each account credited via `DevnetState::credit` (default 10,000 PYDE = 10,000,000,000 quanta, configurable via `--prefund-amount`). **Anvil-style banner**: chain_id (default `31337` — Anvil's "don't replay on mainnet" sentinel), prefund summary, copy-paste-friendly addresses + secrets — stable format for downstream tests to grep. **Long-running wave loop**: `Devnet::run_one_wave` ticks on a configurable interval (`--tick-ms`, default 1000) so `wave_id` advances even with no pending txs. **Graceful Ctrl-C shutdown**: final report prints chain_id + prefund count + waves committed. **Out of scope (follow-up PR)**: JSON-RPC handlers wired to `DevnetState` (`pyde_sendRawTransaction` / `pyde_getBalance` / `pyde_getNonce` / `pyde_getReceipt` / `pyde_call`) — the existing RPC scaffold is wired to the validator's `ConsensusStore`, so the devnet needs a parallel `DevnetState`-backed `RpcContext`. The banner currently shows `RPC server: (not yet wired — follow-up PR)` to set expectations. The `--fork <RPC>` flag (brief A6) is blocked on the state-snapshot protocol shipping. **Test surface**: 8 new runner tests in `devnet::runner::tests` (seed stability + distinctness + banner-hex helper + prefund-state credit + shutdown-signal exit + idle-tick wave progress) + 2 new CLI tests (defaults + custom flags parsing). Node lib total: 355 → 364. Live binary smoke verified: `cargo run --bin pyde -- devnet --tick-ms 100 --prefund-count 3` prints banner + 3 deterministic accounts + runs until Ctrl-C. — PR [#172](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/172)
- [x] **`pyde devnet` JSON-RPC server + `--rpc-listen` flag** — closes the otigen Phase 1 A4 unblock kicked off by #172. The long-running devnet now binds an Anvil-compatible JSON-RPC 2.0 server backed by `DevnetState` so `otigen deploy` against `pyde devnet` works end-to-end. **New flag**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8545` (port matches Anvil/Hardhat so existing wallet libraries work without reconfig); omit for banner-only mode. **5 methods**: `pyde_chainId` (hex u64), `pyde_sendRawTransaction` (borsh-encoded `Tx` hex → tx hash hex; submits + commits one wave so receipt is queryable immediately), `pyde_getBalance` (hex u128), `pyde_getTransactionCount` (hex u64 next nonce derived from `NonceWindow.base + bitmap.trailing_ones()`), `pyde_getTransactionReceipt` (receipt JSON or null). Names track Anvil's `eth_*` shape with the `pyde_` prefix so wallet libs port over by string substitution. **Wire format**: `0x`-prefixed lowercase hex throughout, JSON-RPC 2.0 single + batch + notification handling, standard error codes (`-32700` parse, `-32600` invalid request, `-32601` method not found, `-32602` invalid params, `-32603` internal); notifications get `204 No Content` per spec. **Receipt persistence**: `DevnetState` now stores receipts indexed by `TxHash` (`receipts: HashMap<TxHash, Receipt>` on `Inner`); `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs` inserts as it builds; `get_receipt(&tx_hash)` accessor serves the RPC. **Lifecycle**: RPC server binds up-front (port-conflict errors surface before the banner prints), serves alongside the tick loop under the same shutdown watch, drains cleanly on Ctrl-C; banner shows the live RPC URL when bound, falls back to "(disabled — pass --rpc-listen to enable)" otherwise; final report adds `RPC bound: <addr>`. **Out of scope (separate follow-up PRs)**: `pyde_call` (view calls via `WasmExecutor` — needs a separate context-build path), `pyde_getLogs` (event index), `pyde_blockNumber` (easy add once otigen exercises it), `--fork <RPC>` (brief A6; blocked on snapshot protocol). **Test surface**: 12 new RPC dispatch + handler tests in `devnet::rpc::tests` including an end-to-end `sendRawTransaction → receipt → balance` round trip + error paths (malformed JSON, missing `jsonrpc`, unknown method, bad hex, unknown tx hash) + batch requests + notifications; 1 new runner integration test (`run_devnet_with_rpc_listen_binds_and_reports_addr`) binding `127.0.0.1:0` and asserting on the OS-assigned port. Node lib total: 364 → 377. **Live-verified**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8547` responds to `pyde_chainId` with `0x7a69` (31337) and `pyde_getBalance` with `0x2540be400` (10,000,000,000 quanta default prefund). — PR [#173](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/173)
- [x] **`pyde_waveId` RPC method (devnet)** — Pyde's analogue of EVM `eth_blockNumber`. Pyde uses **wave** not block per the DAG-Mysticeti consensus model (HOST_FN_ABI §7.3 `wave_id`); the RPC method follows. New `DevnetState::current_wave_id()` accessor over `Inner.current_wave` (updated by every `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs`); `pyde_waveId` handler returns hex u64. **2 new tests** — `wave_id_starts_at_zero_before_any_commits` + `wave_id_advances_after_send_raw_transaction` (proves the end-to-end send → commit → query cycle). **Live-verified**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8548 --tick-ms 200` returns hex-encoded wave id that advances over idle ticks. Node lib total: 377 → 379. **The other two A4 RPC extras (`pyde_call` view calls, `pyde_getEvents` event index) remain blocked on devnet WASM-contract deploy support** — the devnet currently uses `DevnetExecutor` (native pre-flight only), so there are no deployed contracts to call against and no events emitted by `pyde::emit_event`. Documented as deferred-with-reason in `devnet/rpc.rs` module docs. Unblocks when devnet swaps in `WasmExecutor` + contract deploy plumbing (its own future workstream — not on the immediate roadmap). — PR [#174](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/174)
- [x] **wasm-exec: revert `pyde::emit_event` to `-> i32` per spec restoration (A11)** — closes engine ask A11 from the otigen Phase 1 brief. Pyde-book commit b816592 (2026-05-28, doc-cleanup) tightened the spec's `emit_event` return type from `-> i32` to `-> ()` as a drive-by along with the (deliberate) variable-length storage redesign. The reclassification wasn't called out in the commit message + wasn't motivated by the storage redesign (events were always variable-length). Reverting restores the deliberate design + preserves the option for v2 (event ordinal, byte count, etc.) without a hard fork + stays consistent with `transfer` which is also a mutating op and `-> i32`. Spec restored (§3.1 imports example + §3.4 return-shape table — §7.5 was never drifted) in paired [pyde-book#211](https://github.com/pyde-net/pyde-book/pull/211). Engine: 4 inline WAT test fixtures pick up `(result i32)` + trailing `drop`; closure returns `Ok(0)` after the existing event push; module-doc updated to reflect `-> i32` + the reservation rationale. Unblocks 10+ otigen example contracts (counter-token, erc20-token, simple-multisig, vesting, merkle-claim-airdrop, etc.) that hadn't migrated. All 223 wasm-exec lib tests green. — PR [#176](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/176)
- [x] **devnet now uses the production validator runtime (no parallel impl)** — closes a deep architectural concern surfaced during the A4 follow-up review: the MC-2 spike's `Devnet` composer + `DevnetExecutor` + `run_smoke` scenario were parallel implementations that diverged from mainnet code paths, and a partial RPC migration was building on top of that divergence. **Fix**: deleted the spike orchestration (`composer.rs`, `executor.rs`, `smoke.rs`, `rpc.rs`, `tests/devnet_smoke.rs` + the `--smoke` CLI mode) and rewrote `devnet/runner.rs` to drive the **production validator runtime** in solo mode. Same `WasmExecutor` (via `WasmExecutorAdapter`), same `DevnetState` mutator (production validator already uses it as StateMutator substitute until the state crate's `commit_wave` lands), same `PydeMempoolView`, same `WaveCommitter`, same `Driver`, same `FalconBeaconScheme` (real PQ FALCON-512 beacon, ephemeral keypair, solo committee = `[self_pk]`). Only the network layer is stubbed: libp2p binds to ephemeral loopback, `producer_quorum = 1`, no peers, no mDNS. **Mainnet-side, non-breaking extension**: new `ValidatorPreRunHook` type (generic `Box<dyn FnOnce(&ValidatorRuntime) + Send>`) + `run_validator_with_hook` / `run_validator_until_ctrl_c_with_hook` variants. The hook fires once between `ValidatorRuntime::build` and task spawn. Production passes `None` — zero behavior change. Future non-devnet uses include A6 state-snapshot loading at boot, integration-test state seeding, monitoring installation. Devnet uses it to pre-fund genesis accounts via `runtime.state.credit(addr, amount)` — pre-funding now rides the production code path, not a devnet-specific side door. **Why this matters**: contract deploy + call + events + everything mainnet supports works on devnet automatically because devnet IS the mainnet flow minus consensus replication + networking. As mainnet matures (DKG ceremony, threshold-decryption execution, remaining 5 of 9 slashable offenses), devnet inherits with no devnet-side work. **Kept (production-load-bearing despite the "devnet" module name)**: `devnet/state.rs` (`DevnetState` — used by `ValidatorRuntime`, `WaveCommitter`, mainloop), `devnet/wallet.rs` (`Wallet` — vertex-producer test + devnet runner). **Devnet glue** (in `crates/node/src/devnet/runner.rs`): tempdir for libp2p keypair + FALCON keypair + ConsensusStore (auto-cleaned on drop, fresh chain per `pyde devnet` start); deterministic devnet validator FALCON secret from `Blake3("pyde-devnet-v1/validator")` (distinct domain from wallet secrets via the `/validator` suffix) so the validator pubkey is stable across restarts; pre-fund closure built from the deterministic wallet seeds, fed through `ValidatorPreRunHook`. **Banner unchanged externally**; internal flow now boots the real validator stack. **CLI**: `--smoke` flag removed; all other devnet flags unchanged (`--prefund-count`, `--prefund-amount`, `--chain-id`, `--tick-ms`, `--rpc-listen` — `--rpc-listen` is a stub this PR, follow-up rewires devnet RPC against the production stack handles so contract deploy + call work end-to-end). **Live-verified**: `pyde devnet --tick-ms 200 --prefund-count 1` boot log shows `devnet: genesis pre-fund applied` (hook fired) + `validator: bound + dialing` (production validator runtime now drives the devnet) + `beacon scheme: FalconBeaconScheme committee_size=1 keypair=ephemeral committee=solo` (real PQ beacon running). 340 node-crate tests pass (was 379 — dropped 39 with the removed spike modules: smoke + composer + executor + rpc + the integration test). — PR [#175](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/175)
- [x] **devnet RPC now wired against the production validator runtime (A4 PR2)** — closes the second half of the A4 follow-up that #175 explicitly deferred. New `devnet/rpc.rs` introduces `DevnetRpcContext` holding `Arc`-cloned production handles: `Arc<DevnetState>` (production state mutator + view), `Arc<PydeMempoolView>` (production mempool with full β.5 validation pipeline), and `Arc<ConsensusStore>` (production RocksDB-backed receipt store). 6 methods land: `pyde_chainId`, `pyde_waveId`, `pyde_sendRawTransaction`, `pyde_getBalance`, `pyde_getTransactionCount`, `pyde_getTransactionReceipt`. RPC server bound inside the `ValidatorPreRunHook` when `--rpc-listen` is supplied — no mainnet-side surface change; the hook is the generic post-build / pre-spawn extension point added in #175. Uses `tokio::signal::ctrl_c` for its own shutdown — same signal the validator binary listens for, so both shut down together. **Production-flow semantics**: unlike the deleted spike's `Devnet::submit_and_commit` ("instant-commit" per call), the production-stack path is async + tick-paced: `PydeMempoolView::insert(tx).await` runs the full validation pipeline (FALCON sig + balance + nonce + chain_id + structural + per-sender rate limit + dedupe) then returns immediately with the canonical tx hash; the production producer task picks up the tx on its next tick (~250 ms) and packs it into a vertex; the committer commits the wave on its next tick (~125 ms); the receipt is queryable via `pyde_getTransactionReceipt` once the wave commits (~250-500 ms after `sendRawTransaction`). otigen + similar clients should poll with ~100 ms backoff — Anvil's "instant-commit" UX is a property of its single-process synchronous executor; Pyde's production stack is event-driven + tick-paced, so devnet inherits that timing. **Why this matters**: contract deploy + call + events automatically work because they go through the production execution path. As mainnet matures (DKG ceremony, threshold-decryption execution, remaining slashable offenses), devnet inherits with no devnet-side work. **Live-verified end-to-end**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8549 --tick-ms 200 --prefund-count 1`: `pyde_chainId` → `0x7a69` (31337), `pyde_waveId` → `0x0` (idle ticks haven't committed yet), `pyde_getBalance` → `0x2540be400` (10,000,000,000 quanta = prefund applied via the production `DevnetState::credit` path). Boot log: `devnet: rpc server bound addr=127.0.0.1:8549` + `validator: bound + dialing` + `beacon scheme: FalconBeaconScheme committee_size=1 keypair=ephemeral committee=solo`. — PR [#177](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/177)

- [x] **wasm-exec: align `pyde::falcon_verify` return to spec (A9)** — closes otigen Phase 1 follow-up A9. [HOST_FN_ABI §7.7](https://book.pyde.network/companion/HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC.html#77-cryptographic-primitives) declares `pyde::falcon_verify` returns `0` for valid + `ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID` (`-17`, §4) for invalid — the 0-is-success convention every other status-code-returning host fn uses. Engine returned the inverted `1`/`0` boolean. **Impact**: any contract following the spec convention (`falcon_verify(...) == 0` to authorize) silently treated invalid signatures as authorized. Concretely: `simple-multisig`, `dao-governance`, every otigen example contract that calls `pyde::falcon_verify` and checks `== 0` for success. Fix: 3 LOC change in `host_fns/crypto.rs` plus import of `pyde_engine_types::error::ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID`; module doc reframed. Two existing end-to-end tests in `executor.rs` updated to assert spec-aligned values: `host_fn_falcon_verify_real_keypair_returns_zero` (was `_returns_one`, WAT traps if return != 0 — uses `if unreachable end` directly on the return value), `host_fn_falcon_verify_tampered_sig_returns_err_signature_invalid` (was `_returns_zero`, WAT compares to `i32.const -17`). Trap semantics for malformed inputs (pubkey/sig rejected by pyde_crypto, oversize msg/sig) unchanged. All 223 wasm-exec lib tests green. Otigen-side follow-up: revert the temporary `"1"` expectation in `runner_engine::tests::phase_e_falcon_dsl_signs_and_verifies_end_to_end` back to `"0"` per the A1 unblock pattern. — PR [#182](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/182)

- [x] **wasm-exec + tx: `handle_standard` contract-call dispatch** — closes the gap where Standard txs targeting contracts (`tx.to` has code) were rejected with `HandlerError::ContractCallDeferred` and never reached the WASM runtime. otigen-test deploy-loop integration test #236 is unblocked end-to-end now. **`CallPayload` wire type**: new `pyde_engine_types::call::CallPayload { function: String, calldata: Vec<u8> }` is the borsh-encoded payload `Tx::data` carries for contract-targeting Standard txs. The chain dispatches by function name (not by 4-byte selector); calldata is the function's args, no selector prefix. **`handle_standard_contract_call`** is the new method on `WasmExecutorAdapter` that owns the contract-call execution — pre-routed from the dispatcher when `accounts.code_hash(&tx.to)` returns `Some`, so the tx-crate's `handle_standard` never sees a contract target in the production path. **Flow** (12 steps): decode `CallPayload` → load + verify sender (auth + nonce + balance) → ensure module cached (`load_from_persistent` for cold-restart from a snapshot) → find function in ABI by name → attribute checks (`CONSTRUCTOR` lockout, non-`PAYABLE` refuses value) → pre-debit sender + commit nonce → build `TxOverlay` + credit value to contract via overlay → build `HostContext` with `self_address = tx.to`, `input = payload.calldata` → `execute_call(&code_hash, &payload.function, ctx)` → on clean exit finalise overlay; on trap/revert/OOG drop overlay (no state changes persist) → Receipt with the call's `return_data`. **Failure model**: pre-execution rejects charge `MIN_GAS_LIMIT` (the intrinsic floor); post-execution reverts charge `tx.gas_limit` (no refund per PIP-4). The sender's pre-debit at step 6 stays forfeit on any post-execution revert. **`handle_standard` cleanup**: removes the `ContractCallDeferred` short-circuit (the dispatcher's pre-route handles contract targets upstream); the tx-crate handler now sees only the value-transfer path. Removes the `HandlerError::ContractCallDeferred` variant entirely; the old `contract_call_path_returns_deferred` test becomes `contract_target_treated_as_plain_value_transfer` (direct callers of the handler get pure value-transfer semantics when they bypass the dispatcher). **Tests**: `standard_call_into_no_op_function_succeeds` (deploy + call happy path); `standard_call_to_unknown_function_reverts` (function not in ABI); `standard_call_to_constructor_at_runtime_reverts` (`CONSTRUCTOR` lockout); `standard_call_with_value_to_non_payable_function_reverts` (`PAYABLE` attribute enforcement); `standard_call_contract_revert_charges_full_gas_and_keeps_pre_debit` (`(unreachable)` trap; full gas_limit charged; pre-debit stays); `contract_target_treated_as_plain_value_transfer` (direct callers of tx-crate handle_standard). Types crate: 89 → 92. Wasm-exec crate: 254 → 259. Tx crate: 231 → 231 (1 renamed + variant tests adjusted). Workspace all-green; clippy clean. — PR [#205](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/205)
- [x] **wasm-exec: wire constructor execution into `handle_deploy`** — completes the deploy slice. `handle_deploy` now invokes the contract's constructor function via `WasmExecutor::execute_call` when the ABI declares one, with full rollback semantics on revert / trap / OOG. **Flow change**: step 8 is now a pre-debit + overlay-stage (writes the contract account into a `TxOverlay` rather than directly to `AccountStore`). Step 9 invokes `execute_call(&code_hash, constructor_name, ctx)` if `abi.constructor_index` is `Some`; on constructor failure the overlay is dropped (contract account vanishes, sstore writes vanish, `tx.value` is forfeited per PIP-4's no-refund policy) and the receipt carries the full `gas_limit` as `gas_used` (constructor ran). On success the overlay is finalised in one batch. Step 10 is `register_name` and step 11 persists the deployer's pre-debit. The handler still returns a `Reverted` Receipt with floor gas charged for any pre-execution failure (decode, name validation, wasm validation, balance check, sender not found). Contracts with no constructor (`abi.constructor_index == None`) skip the constructor call entirely; `init_calldata` in the envelope is silently ignored in that case (the wasm couldn't observe what it didn't import). **HostContext for the constructor**: built with `self_address = derived contract address`, `tx.input = deploy.init_calldata`, `tx.value = tx.value`; the overlay handle is threaded in for storage host fns, and the executor handle for `cross_call`; `wave_timestamp = 0` (orchestrator patches in prod). `execute_call` is the right entry point — `execute_contract_call` explicitly rejects `CONSTRUCTOR`-attributed functions with `ERR_CONSTRUCTOR_LOCKOUT` (callable only at deploy time). **Tests**: `deploy_runs_no_op_constructor_to_success` (empty-body constructor runs cleanly + commits the contract + registers the name); `deploy_constructor_revert_rolls_back_contract_account_and_name` (constructor uses `(unreachable)`; receipt is `Reverted` with full `gas_limit` charged; the contract account never persists + the name registry stays empty); `deploy_no_constructor_path_still_succeeds` (regression gate on the existing test against the constructor-execution change); all existing deploy tests pass unchanged. Helper `wasm_with_constructor(body)` builds a wasm whose ABI declares a constructor at index 0 with the given WAT body. Wasm-exec tests: 251 → 254. - [x] **account + wasm-exec: name-based contract addresses + `DeployData`-driven `handle_deploy`** — closes the spec drift in the deploy flow where the existing `handle_deploy` decoded `tx.data` as raw WASM bytes and derived the contract address via CREATE-style `Poseidon2(deployer || nonce)`. The spec (per the `address-naming-collision` design memo) routes contracts through ENS-style unique names instead: `address = Poseidon2("pyde-contract:" || name)` with a registry-uniqueness gate. `tx.data` is the borsh-encoded `DeployData` envelope (name + wasm_bytes + contract_type + init_calldata). **Address derivation**: new `pub const CONTRACT_ADDRESS_PREFIX = b"pyde-contract:"` domain separator + `pub fn contract_name_address(name) -> Address` = `Poseidon2(prefix || name_bytes)` in `crates/account/src/address.rs`. **`handle_deploy` flow** (13 steps replacing the prior 10-step CREATE-style): (1) decode `tx.data` as `DeployData` envelope (reject malformed), (2) validate name via `names::validate_name` (length + char-set rules), (3) reject if name already registered, (4) validate wasm bundle via the existing `validate_deploy` pipeline (ABI + import allowlist + attrs), (5) derive address via `contract_name_address(name)`, (6) verify deployer balance covers `value + gas`, (7) compile + persist WASM via `compile_and_persist`, (8) materialise `Contract` account at derived address, (9) `register_name(name, address)` writes both-leg atomic mapping, (10) move value deployer → contract, (11) commit deployer's nonce, (12) debit `gas_limit × base_fee` (no refunds per PIP-4), (13) Receipt with `return_data = contract_address.bytes`. Constructor invocation (`init_calldata` execution via `WasmExecutor::execute_call("init", ...)`) stays deferred to the next slice. - [x] **tx + node: cross-repo Tx canonical-hash parity test + fix devnet wallet pre-image bug (A17)** — closes engine ask A17 from the otigen Phase 1 brief. **Parity test**: new `crates/tx/tests/wire_format_parity.rs` reads otigen's fixture (`otigen-tx-codec/fixtures/cross_repo_tx_vectors_v1.json`) and for each vector materialises the JSON input into a real `pyde_engine_types::tx::Tx`, computes the canonical hash via `pyde_engine_tx::tx_hash`, asserts byte-equality against `expected_tx_hash_hex`, decodes `sample_wire_bytes_hex` via `borsh::from_slice<Tx>` and re-computes the hash from the decoded `Tx` (covers encode → decode → re-encode round-trip), and verifies `sample_signature_hex` back-verifies under the pinned pubkey via `verify_hash_signature` (proves engine accepts otigen-produced sigs end-to-end). - [x] **node: `SlashSubmitter` bridges equivocation detection to on-chain slash (validator lifecycle PR-3)** — third PR in the consolidation slice. **Closes the "safety detectors are paper tigers" gap.** Until now the slashing-detector consumers (`EquivocationConsumer`, `BadStateRootSigConsumer`, etc.) called `Slasher::record()` which only updated the in-memory offense log + jail map. The on-chain `ValidatorRecord.stake` reduction happens only via `TxType::Slash` — and nothing was submitting one automatically. So safety detectors were detection-only: equivocations were observed and logged locally, but no validator ever lost stake on-chain. **`SlashSubmitter`** closes that gap for `EquivocationConsumer`. After each successful in-memory record, the consumer looks up the offender's FALCON pubkey via the injected `CommitteeLookup` (v1: `StaticCommitteeLookup` — position-indexed `Vec<Option<FalconPubkey>>` built from genesis-committee config), pulls the prior equivocating vertex from `VertexStore` by hash, builds a `SafetyEvidence` with both vertices' pre-image bytes + FALCON sigs, signs a `TxType::Slash` with the local validator's `FalconKeypair` (setting itself as `reporter` — collects 20% reporter share per `Offense::Equivocation.spec().distribution.reporter_bps`), and inserts into the local mempool via `PydeMempoolView::insert`. The chain-side `handle_slash` (PR-2) then reduces stake + transitions the offender to `Status::Jailed`. **Wiring + opt-in**: `with_slash_submitter(submitter)` is an opt-in builder so older consumer tests that don't spin up a mempool keep working in detection-only mode; two new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`equivocation_consumer_slash_tx_submitted` / `_failed`). **Newly public**: `consensus::vertex_sig_pre_image` (was `pub(crate) pre_hash_bytes`) — exposes the canonical FALCON pre-image bytes so the submitter routes both ends of the evidence through one encoding source; the chain-side `handle_slash` hashes the same bytes via `verify_hash_signature`. **Out of scope (PR-3b/c follow-ups)**: same shape for `BadStateRootSig` / `BadAnchorAttestation` / `InvalidVertexStructure` (PR-3b); Liveness consumers like `ExtendedDowntime` need a distinct `LivenessEvidence` variant since the auto-detected liveness pipeline has no per-event FALCON sig pair (PR-3c); validator runtime wiring that passes the submitter into the consumer at startup needs the genesis-committee → lookup build path (deferred to a runtime-side PR that doesn't touch consumer logic). **Tests**: 6 new on `slash_submitter` — 3 on `StaticCommitteeLookup` resolution paths; `build_equivocation_slash_tx_produces_chain_verifiable_evidence` (end-to-end build with real FALCON-signed vertices, asserts the produced evidence verifies under real `falcon_verify` — the chain-side invariant); `build_equivocation_slash_tx_rejects_unknown_offender` (defensive guard on missing committee mapping); `build_equivocation_slash_tx_surfaces_missing_prior_vertex` (defensive guard on pruned `VertexStore`). Existing `EquivocationConsumer` tests migrated from `#[test]` to `#[tokio::test]` (dispatch is now async). Node-crate lib tests: 377 → 383. Workspace all-green; clippy clean. — PR [#199](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/199)
- [x] **tx: `handle_slash` reads `Offense` from evidence + branches jail vs exit (validator lifecycle PR-2)** — second PR in the consolidation slice. `handle_slash` previously hardcoded a 10% slash + `Status::Exited` transition for every Safety offense, ignoring the per-offense penalties in the slashing crate's catalog. This PR wires the catalog through end-to-end. **Changes**: `SafetyEvidence` gains an `offense: Offense` field; new `HandlerError::SlashOffenseClassMismatch` rejects Liveness offenses via the Safety shape (Liveness evidence ships in PR-3 alongside the auto-submit pipeline); slash amount now reads `record.stake × spec.first_instance_bps / 10_000` (Equivocation/BadStateRootSig stay at 10%; BadAnchorAttestation/InvalidVertexStructure/BadDecryptionShare move to their catalog 5%); distribution reads from `spec.distribution` — `SAFETY_DEFAULT` (50% burn / 30% treasury / 20% reporter) now credits both reporter AND treasury via `treasury_address()`, while `ALL_BURN` (InvalidVertexStructure) trivially zeros both shares; status transition branches on `spec.jail_epochs` — `> 0` → `Status::Jailed` with `jail_until_wave = wave + jail_epochs × EPOCH_LENGTH_WAVES`, `== 0` leaves status unchanged (warning-only path, currently unreachable from SafetyEvidence but kept for future Safety additions); `TOTAL_ACTIVE_STAKE_WEIGHTED` decrements only on `Active → Jailed` since Unbonding already decremented at StakeWithdraw time (re-decrementing would cause saturating-sub underflow); `REPORTER_REWARD_BPS` bumped 1000 → 2000 to match `SAFETY_DEFAULT`. **Spec evolution**: SLASHING.md treats Safety as 1-epoch jail with fractional slash, not the original "100% + permanent ban" baseline — the latter is v2 hardening (correlation multiplier + repeat-offense scaling). **Tests**: 229 → 231 (+2 net). - [x] **tx: add `Status::Jailed` variant + `jail_until_wave` field to `ValidatorRecord` (validator lifecycle PR-1)** — first PR in the validator-lifecycle consolidation slice. The chain-state `ValidatorRecord` previously had only `Active` / `Unbonding` / `Exited` — no `Jailed` state at all. Per the slashing-rules-catalog, Safety offenses transition to `Exited` (permanent), while Liveness-with-jail offenses (`ExtendedDowntime`, `DkgParticipationFailure`, `DecryptionShareWithholding`) need a finite-jail state that returns to `Active` via `Unjail`. - [x] **node: validator `FalconKeypair` uses real FALCON-512 (A16 part 2)** — closes the validator-side half of otigen Phase 1 follow-up A16. #195 migrated the devnet `Wallet` (tx signing) to real FALCON via `consensus::FalconSigner`; this PR migrates the disk-backed `FalconKeypair` (vertex signing) so the validator producer / mainloop / beacon hot paths all run on the same crypto end-to-end. Removes the last `MockSigner`-backed signing surface on the validator binary. **File format v1 → v2**: on-disk shape changes from `(version: u8 = 1, secret: 32 bytes mock seed, pubkey: 897 bytes Blake3-extended mock)` to `(version: u8 = 2, secret: 32 bytes FALCON keygen seed, pubkey: 897 bytes real FALCON-512)`. v1 mock keypairs are rejected with `MismatchedVersion` — operators with v1 keypairs regenerate (the old keypair never reached production validators, so the upgrade path is "delete the file"). Persisting a 32-byte seed (not the 1281-byte FALCON secret key bytes) keeps the on-disk footprint small + leans on `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_keygen_deterministic` to re-derive the keypair on every load; the persisted pubkey is then cross-checked against the freshly-derived one as the integrity gate. **`FalconKeypair::from_seed(seed) -> Result<Self, FalconKeypairError>`**: deterministic constructor mirroring `FalconSigner::from_seed` (#195) — same seed → same `(pk, sk)` across restarts. New `FalconKeypairError::Keygen(String)` variant surfaces the (effectively unreachable) upstream-keygen failure. The old `from_mock_secret` name is retained as a thin panicking shim that delegates to `from_seed` so existing devnet-runner call sites compile through the migration; it'll be retired in the follow-up renaming pass. **Sig non-determinism**: real FALCON-512 sigs are non-deterministic per the FN-DSA spec (fresh randomness per sign — guards against fault-injection attacks). Tests that previously asserted byte-equality of two sigs over the same pre-image (`save_and_load_round_trip_preserves_pubkey_and_signature`, `from_mock_secret_is_deterministic`) now assert under-pubkey verification instead via `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_verify` — verifier contract is what matters, not byte-identical outputs. The runtime sig-length assertion in `runtime::tests::falcon_keypair_signs_through_signer_trait` widens from a 666-byte exact match to the `[500, 1000]` FALCON wire-format range. Old `signer_impl_matches_mock_signer_with_same_secret` test is replaced with `signer_impl_produces_real_falcon_verifiable_sigs` since the keypair no longer wraps `MockSigner` — the verifier contract is what's load-bearing. The `derive_mock_pubkey` Blake3-stretching helper goes away with the migration. **Test counts**: 17 `falcon_keypair::tests` (was 14 — added `from_mock_secret_alias_matches_from_seed`, replaced two sig-equality tests with verify-under-pubkey shapes); 377 node-crate lib tests pass total (was 376). Workspace all-green, clippy clean. **Otigen unblocks**: validator binary now uses real FALCON across every signing surface (vertex via `FalconKeypair`, beacon via `BeaconKeypair`, devnet wallet via `Wallet` from #195) — `pyde devnet` no longer surfaces any mock-vs-real split internally, honouring the `devnet_should_be_anvil_simple` memory principle in the small. Closes the A16 work-stream end-to-end. — PR [#196](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/196)
- [x] **node + consensus: devnet `Wallet` uses real FALCON-512 + Poseidon2 address (A16 part 1)** — closes the wallet-side half of otigen Phase 1 follow-up A16. Pyde's principle (per the `devnet_should_be_anvil_simple` memory: "don't surface internal mock-vs-real-FALCON splits as user-facing choices") is "same crypto everywhere across mainnet / testnet / devnet". Current state violated that: chain verification was already real FALCON (`pyde_engine_tx::verify_tx_signature` → `pyde_crypto::falcon_verify`) but the devnet wallet signed with `MockSigner` (Blake3 counter-rehash) and derived addresses as `Blake3(secret)` not `Poseidon2(falcon_pubkey)`. That blocked otigen-wallet (which already uses real FALCON) from importing devnet wallets without a parallel mock-FALCON code path. This PR catches up the wallet side. Validator-side `FalconKeypair` (vertex signing) stays on `MockSigner` — separate follow-up (A16 part 2). **Companion change**: pyde-crypto#1 shipped `falcon_keygen_deterministic(seed)` — wraps the upstream's `FnDsaKeyPair::generate_deterministic` for the "same seed → same keypair across restarts" guarantee. **`consensus::signer::FalconSigner`**: production `Signer` impl wrapping `pyde_crypto::FalconSecretKey` + the derived public key; built via `FalconSigner::from_seed(&[u8; 32])` which calls `falcon_keygen_deterministic`; `sign` delegates to `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_sign`; falls back to a representative-length zero signature on the impossible upstream failure path so the chain verify rejects deterministically rather than panicking. **`devnet::wallet::Wallet`**: `signer: MockSigner` → `signer: FalconSigner`; address derivation `Blake3(secret)` → `Poseidon2(falcon_pubkey)` (production formula per HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC §3.7); new `pubkey_bytes()` accessor surfaces the 897-byte FALCON pubkey for callers (banner, future auth-keys registration). **Devnet banner**: prints a 16-byte FALCON-pk prefix per prefunded account as visual confirmation real FALCON is in use; secret stays full 32 bytes so otigen-wallet's `--from-devnet` import can re-derive the full keypair via the same `falcon_keygen_deterministic` API. **Tests**: 4 new `FalconSigner` unit tests in `consensus::signer` (deterministic pubkey across calls; different seeds diverge; sig verifies under real `falcon_verify`; pubkey is 897 bytes); wallet tests updated for new shape (`signature_matches_independent_sign_of_pre_image` → `signature_verifies_under_wallet_pubkey` since FALCON sigs are non-deterministic per-sign per spec — verifier contract is what matters, not byte-identical sig outputs; `build_transfer_signs_with_wallet_signer` → `..._produces_falcon_sig_in_expected_size_range` since FALCON sigs are variable-length 500..=1000 bytes); `generate_prefunded_returns_requested_count` asserts `Poseidon2(falcon_pubkey)` derivation. `cargo test -p pyde-engine-consensus --lib signer::` 8 passed. `cargo test -p pyde-engine-node --lib` 376 passed.
